O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, most dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the last of medical science together with its fulfillment, and I have finished it with its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete this treatise for you, which is part of the work by hand, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work by hand is treated in our region and is strange from all over, it is a worthy science and appropriate, and it is not delayed from the fire more than the small descriptions in books of the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, there has come error and vanity, and the intentions are closed, and the science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me seems that I shall add to it the order of this healer in accordance with the path of exposure and statement and abbreviation; and will come together with the shapes of the tools for cauterization, and other instruments for the work, with the adjustment of the statement and preparation of it, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our land, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who deals with it to surmount in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and the shapes and connections and separations of the vessels, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of vessels, and the movement and rest of the joints, and the place of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason it is said that nothing is with the good, and without the bad, and with work there is danger; and most of all in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say to you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not familiar with the above mentioned things, let him beware that he does not err and harm others; so that I have often wanted many of those who meddle in this science and who abandon themselves to theory and not to experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish man who cut an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries at the base of the neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another foolish man who caught a stone from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took it out with him and killed himself in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also seen him called to pull out a stone from the bladder of a woman, and I saw the appearance of the disease and the size of the stone; and if he had pulled it out, he would have died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see another mirth who took in cure a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound. And the mirror plain of ignorance draws out the break on the wound with very strong medicine, leaving no scar to the wound, and leaves it thus.i. finished; and he commanded that he did not unfasten it at all; and delayed so that his leg was completely gone and the toes came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I had dislocated it, he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of corruption were confirmed in him or his member, and he could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to go away by the member until the members were completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another mirth who broke apart.i. abscess that was infected, and then set it on fire with the evil of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is infected with melancholic humor, it must only be touched with iron if it is not in its natural place so that all that is corrupted can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, good son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into 1.2 divisions: that is to say, work in which there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each of these in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason, you must guard yourself so that the foolish man cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your arms in confidence, and undertake your diseases lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are loosed; and remove your weapons from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galleons gives some of his admonitions: "Do not take on as your own work the healing of a sick person unless you are called to do so."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to II. chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are on fire cautery and water-based medicine, and the order of the limbs; and the forms of instruments, and the iron instruments for cauterizing, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are on cutting and piercing, and sucking out wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things; and the order of the chapters and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torments, and similar things; and it prescribes the use of a pole for support up to the hip, and the shape of tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, we remember the work; it is necessary that I explain the quality of help and the harm of each complexio
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest word and subtlest science and its reply hidden; and many wise men would speak on this, and agree with it; and I am lacking in words, for I shorten them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire is helpful to all complexions when it has matter; otherwise, it is not. That is to say, a complexio
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In warm and dry complexions together the matter, no one devised and said that cautery is great help; and another said the opposite: that cautery does not deserve to be used for diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used by hot disease caused by heat, nor by dryness; and he who said the opposite that cautery does great help to hot and dry diseases that come in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man with his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And any path, does not interfere but that who has experienced it, and who knows by long practice the use of the cautery paste, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the remedies and the space of time; we do not fear others' complexions, nonetheless with cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all that should be gathered and agree to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that combined fire cautery is more effective than hot medicine in treating secrets and many other illnesses.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes not forth except to the limb which it burns, and harms no other member so much.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by removal, and bring disease of harm to the member for cure; and perhaps they cause illness.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its height and because of the goodness of its substance, does not cause heat, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experiment and because of the length of my service and of the study that I have employed in this art, and it is based on the veracity of things; and therefore I ask forgiveness for the length of speech, since I do not like to deprive you of the secret which is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, as the philosopher explains in demonstrating; take it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that these cauterizations should be made at a certain time, and they should be performed while praying.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the harmful effects that may arise due to the help of cauterization; and most especially, the cauterization is for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait until the time when greater harm may come upon the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And I do not think at all, son, as they do so foolishly; for when a disease is cured by cauterization, there is no return to the former state; and that is how it should be done; but it is not like what they think; for cauterization is only medicine that changes the appearance, drying up the humors which cause pain, and is more effective than medicine in terms of speed of action, and due to its excellence and dignity.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And one may choose that the disease never returns according to the appearance of the illness and its place and virtue; and superfluities are gathered in it by the acquisition of meat and similar things; unless cauterization is administered at the right time when there is little surplus and moisture, as is done for pain, and for similar things, and the pain does not return; but that happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not hear for the reason that the remedies are called the derrières of medicine, and this is seen; but they do not believe that the remedies are worth anything after medicine, but their intentions are false, and these are the derrières of medicine because when we administer ways to cure in no disease and they are not worth it, then let us administer the remedy, and it is worth it.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Now, although remedies are the derrières of medicine, do not hear them according to the intentions of foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients used to say that a gold-based remedy is more effective than one made of iron, and they only spoke about the quality of gold and its high value; they said that the edges of remedies do not cause inflammation, but this is not true because I have tested it, and I have found that in certain people they do; and a gold remedy is more effective than an iron one, as they used to say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And wherever you heat gold-based instruments, you will not be able to tell if they are too hot or not just by their color, and they can quickly cool down; and if you heat them too much, they will burn on the fire; and so there is enough hesitation.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you should read this chapter up to the part about the eye, so that it is easier for you to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is useful for the head, especially for the brain, and for the ears. It also helps with many ailments, including those caused by cold, such as paralysis, sodom, and apoplexy; and it can also help with pain in the dens and throat, and with many other diseases caused by cold.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a solitive medicine which purifies the head.iii. times or iiij., according to what the virtue and the eagerness and the acostumance of the patient can bear; and then do again the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then put the cross between your hands, and place your palms on the roots of his neck; after that put his two roots, if it bleeds, then heat the fire which is called "olivaire", from which comes this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then put the cross between your hands, and place your palms on the roots of his neck; after that put his two roots, if it bleeds, then heat the fire which is called "olivaire", from which comes this form:
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And then put the cross between your hands, and place your palms on the roots of his neck; after that put his two roots, if it bleeds, then heat the fire which is called  "olivaire", from which comes this form:
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that one should let the cautery burn so much of the bone that it is burned, and then resect what is burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said that one must let the cautery burn so much of the bone, and then resect what is burned from the bone, and be cured; and that one must open the wound very wide, as women put in their needles to cause the humors to come out; and it must be kept open for a long time; after it must be cured and dressed.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good in all cases; for in some men where there is a tendency to pain; and I believe that I should let it burn; for the head bone is weakened by continuous solutions due to nature, as we witness with other limbs; and even when the head bone is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterizing seems more safe and milder to me, and so I use it in the assembly in all cases.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all the head comes chronic pain and lasts a long time, then you must use the yeris of the patient and pills which are called "cochie", and head purgation and oils and poultices; and if one does the fire cautery which we have just said, and it is not good.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of a strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize him slightly as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making the fire cautery on each horn of the head, as we have said above, and making the "vasselz" cautery where one puts the leeches; and it is good that you hold your hand so that you do not see the bone at all: The patient feels too much pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it later; and it is good that the cornes cauterizes be more subtle than those of which one makes the cautery of the head's moieneteit, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the cautery of the head.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the neck comes sudden pain, and is spread to the oil, and the head is purged with medicines mondifian, and other cures have been done that I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not benefit: then make cauterizes according to .ij. ways, that is to say, with medicine water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	When the medicine water cautery does not work, take a piece of almond wood, and cut off the bark and the top, and then make two holes in it, and then put on cotton plunged in oil until it dries out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the medicine ointment has been applied until it is well, and if you see that some of the medicine burners that I have written or treated with medicines burners do not work.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery if it is according to this way: Heat the cauterizer in which this is the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparence; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.

And called "close" because the chief is made in the form of a clo or there is .i. poc corbeure, and in the middle with a small appearance; and put it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly a little, until half of the keur's flesh is burned; and release your hand that the artery does not burn, which is old, and runs an abundance of blood.
de emigraine	de emigraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure the emigraine as we have said in the division of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cautery before spoken of is taken from the medicine and of the iron does not sufice to it; then you must heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and thus sign as soon as a half-inch line is drawn on the painful spot, and hold your hand once, and turn it so that you do not cover the artery and that you do not come to the mandible when it is swallowed, and that the muscle does not move when it is moved, and you guard against the pain of the blood that comes from the artery when it is covered, or coming with great fear to those who do not know it, and who are students and experienced; and leave the work in half a line; but I will tell you how to stop the pain when the artery is covered, and I will show you where it affects in this book.

de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	torture which must be cured by fire is only good for those that move because of fluid, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not use fire on similar things that come from sweat and dander of dogs.

Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the form of the scalpel that we have put before, but it is a little more subtle and it is worth that the blade is a little thicker; after curating the place as I said before, until it is healthy.

de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy

de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistulas by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and dip cotton wicks in oil of rose or juice of pepperwort over oil; then heat the cauterizer; and hold it to the scalp as if in the shape of a feather, together with the tip being the cauterizer; if you see, so point out from one scalp to the other, and if you do not see, so as a tent; but nevertheless, it is necessary that it be held on the scalp.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open, and treat the porosity, and dry it; and if it is closed, so work on it, and then apply fire to the part with oil; put the cauterizer in the oil fat, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to cauterize up to the bone, it would be good. If not, begin cauterizing again, and if you need more, leave it .iij. days; after i put cotton moistened in oil on the wound, and treat with drying ointment until it is healthy, and if .xl. days pass without being healthy, then put on medicine that corrodes until the bone is exposed; and make a cure according to what has come out in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	I have a way of cauterizing the fistula that no one of the ancients has spoken of. Know what a fistula is, and open the place; then put in the opening 1/4 pound of very thin caugh, so that it is this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and i make the quantity of an 1/4 pound; and hold your hand firmly where the caugh is, so that it does not move at all, so that the melted caugh does not run into its oil; and you must put cotton moistened in oil on the wound, at the fistula's opening, and it will be cured by a wonderful cure.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery that we have said, it is good. If not, you must pierce the nose, and bring back the fistula to the nose's own place.

de la dolor des dens	of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or it is cold in the mouth, and medicines have no effect, then it is necessary to use one of two methods of treatment: fire cautery and butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent. Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery together if it is such that you squeeze a ring of iron or of rain, and be large so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the sick; after heat the cauterizer, for from this it will take shape then, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand as long as the cautery is cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be increased that day or the next. de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of both sides
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere. If you are unsure, apply two or three cauterizations according to the strength and quantity of the remedy that the patient can bear; and always use the cauterization knife technique:

tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, or from a fall or injury, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medicine for it is not effective, then it should be burned with fire that is called 'poins', and the burn should be made according to the length of the limb, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its virtue, and its location from torments, and its pain. If it heals after one burn, that's good; but if not, then make another burn on top of that one, for such is custom, so that you should make the burns as long as the patient remains ill.
de meselerie	of healing
