Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And if it is scattered everywhere, it will lose manifestly; so if you cauterize it with those cauteries which we have said to the head, and that is to say, one cautery in his nose, and two cauteries on the lips of the neck, and seven cauteries on the spine, and a great one on the back, and another delicacy, and two on the shoulders, and two on the ribs, and two on each hand, and on the creases of the hands; and keep yourself from burning the nerves that are under the wrist, lest they burn; and do not ever make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, or on the bone of the chest, or on the liver. Know that when you make more cauteries, you will do more help, and it will profit you; and know that the patient does not feel the pain of the cautery as much as the healthy one feels it, because his body is already very corrupt. And it should be that the cautery is large or small according to the members and joints, according to what you shall find in a way with iron. After that, cure him with flour of times with honey and other cures until he is well.
de enfleure	de enfleurer
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When the swelling comes in any member and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, it is not yet healthy, then the fire cautery must be performed on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be a little entering into the flesh of the cure; then let it be oiled until it is healthy. And never is cautery done, with hand or foot, or back, at the exit of the nerve that silences the member, so is the swelling osseous; and yet there enters nothing if he knows not the members and exits of nerves moving the body.
de albaras	de albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is aggravated, and the medicine does not help, then a fire cautery must be performed with a precise cauterizer, according to the amount of flesh around the affected area, until the blight is exposed, and its color changes; then cure it with flour, oil, and plantain leaves, and wormwood and almond juice, each in equal parts; mix them together, wrap them in a cloth, and apply heat until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	For the cure of the plague by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the ulcer appears at the beginning, and you stop up the sight, if the fire cautery is done on the circumference of the ulcer. And all the wise men will tell you that a cauterization should also be made in the middle of the ulcer; but to me this does not seem good, because I fear that it may become inflamed and corrupted, and I have never wanted to do so; and a more correct thing is that it be cauterized around, at the circumference, as we said for many fire cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For some people have a disease that is called "adubelati", and it takes a long time to die, or because of the excess fluid it produces, or because of the age of the patient when it is very old, and it has little blood, or because of the heat of the disease; and you see him hurry to die: then cauterize him all around with small fire cauterizations while poking; then let it be like that. Because it will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you pierce it all the way with the fire cauterization, make the fire cauterization very hot so that this is its shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And hold your hand in the middle of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauterization has completely healed, and make such cauterizations that the patient feels a distance from it in some way so that the course of the pus is chosen. After the cure, as long as he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease that is called "corrodens", and is nothing but a mixture of members, because it eats the members as fire dries them up. If you see this disease in its beginning, which can be treated with fire cauterization, then heat the cauterizations small and large, according to what suits the place where the disease is; after the fire cauterization on all sides until you have healed all corruption, and there remains nothing of it, that all corruption is not taken away. And then leave it for .iij. days, and put oil on the cauterized places so that the burns from the fire are healed, and all corruption. After the cure with medicines that generate heat, in place of fire cauterization; but fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said about the cure with medicines that generate heat in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the porcellains that come from the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Mouth times has come that the pies by default do not give a disease which is called "close" according to our intention, and it is a gross faulted thing that bleeds the foot. And the treatments of this disease are according to 2 ways. It is known cautery of fire, and cautery of hot water. Cautery of fire is so that you heat up 1 cauldron as well like what is a pen of vault, and it is made of good iron to the measure that it can push the nail from all sides, and there are subtle margins; after it put everything hot on the nail, and return your hand completely around the nail until it comes to the bottom of the nail; and leave it in this way 1 day as long as it begins to go corruption; then he does a plaster of wild thistle crushed with string, and leaves the plaster on all night, and the nails will chomp and be uprooted from their roots. Then cure the sore by charging as much as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted by default the body, and many times has come and in hands and em pies, then you must put cautery of hot water; and it is a third way: take a stick of copper or iron, or a pen of vault, and put on the nail and the athenol, that is to say porrells warts; and put the stick on so that it turns red all around, then you put a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the margin of the stick comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water route deep until the root; and allow the disease a little the sting of the hot water an hour; then leave it, and it will be uprooted all its roots. So do one after another, as long as you have cured all these that are in the body, then cure the sores that cause char.
li cure dou trembler	And cure the trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	Here is the translation of the text:
des pustules puans	for the pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	For when the body is covered with pustules that appear from large corrupted matter. If it is necessary at first when they appear to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a delicate cautery made from fern, whose tip is held in fire, or from the root of a plant called aristeola, or with a lens-shaped cautery. And never make the cauterisation at the beginning when they appear, according to this method; and it cannot grow any more pus, but is healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	For when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Maitres avient grant decorremens de sang de l'artere qui est coupe a la plaie que vient au parchemin, ou a l'incision de l'apotheme, ou au cautere du membre, et a les semblanches choses; et est mout grief chose d'estenchir.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Many times there is a great discharge of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the parchment, or to the incision of the abscess, or to the cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a very painful thing to stop. And yet when any one of them happens, if you hurry to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it a little so that the blood does not gush out any more; then put fire to the olive cauterys, great and small, as long as they are all red; then take 2 ounces, or more or less according to the wound and its place, considering that the artery is blocked, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery in place until the blood stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if he catches fire when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished; then take quickly another cautery that is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop making one after another as long as the blood is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is delicate, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when the artery is cut short, it cannot be stopped well unless by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it has not yet been treated, or by tightly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and strained carefully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who shall administer such a tight bandage of cloth or burning things upon it, or other similar things, unless he takes advantage of this?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has neither mirred nor presented medicine, then he must put his two fingers upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and firmly stretch it over the wound and the vein; and do not move them but moisten them with cold water repeatedly until the blood is frozen and thickened and stretched; and make incisions in advance where cauterization and medicine are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which fire cauterization, burning medicine, and the forms of cauterization are appropriate; and I have placed that chapter at the beginning, and I will go on from there in this chapter by the same route as before for those who wish to test it more lightly than those who seek a cure.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I have begun to speak of this, it is necessary that you learn that with this ointment there is more danger and fear than with the first cautery, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to take any foolishness into account. For in many cases people come for treatment. If they come from those who, because of their illness, have died easily due to the violence with which they have endured their illness and the greatness of their ill fortune; and from these one must fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of those who give you their advice and say: "Wait, I am dying"; and the illness is treacherous. It is not appropriate that you consent to such people who come to you who have this way; but put more trust in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open your doors foolishly but carefully, for those of whom you are certain, and from whom you could have gained something, and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation may be converted. And such a one will aid you in acquiring good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Three holy sons, our lords give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you would like to breathe life into the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered you this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to the one before and after the chapter of the cauterizes, which I have devised from the beginning up to the middle, so that you may find more easily that which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	I know that this disease often comes to children in infancy, and when the baby cries too much, it pulls the head of the child; and there is never a response to this reason that one does not understand.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen die quickly; therefore it seems to me that I should slow down the work of this chapter a little in the cures.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulders were wet with water, and each day the head became heavier so that it could not be supported; and because of the moisture, he died, and this moisture came together between the shoulder blade and the rib cage, between the breastbone and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture comes together between the breastbone and the bone, and the ribs are small, then you should cut a wide hole in the head with the edge of the chisel; and be so far away as 12 inches, until the moisture runs; and see this form of the chisel:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross with this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is behind the bone, and the signs that you see are that the joints of the head are opened from each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand on the inside, and it does not respond to you: then you should cut three cuts in the shape:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture. After drawing out the bandages and powders, put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that for five days; then take it off, treating the wound with tar and ointments, and let the head be drawn out equally, and feed the patient dried meat of little moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to incise is that you look at the opening of the anus, and the gathering of the urine; for it is never before; never behind; never on the right; and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So then cut at the opening of the anus, and the discharge of urine, and deal with it according to what you can do; and guard against covering the artery; and bring forth blood, so that the patient dies from a burst vessel and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of remedy
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is a disease that is called "cataract" in the eye or the kidney, and the disease is old age, and the medicine does not benefit, then the following remedy is: cauterize with what you cover the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you have covered the eyes, let the patient rub his forehead with a rough cloth until the arteries show, then extract the patient's neck from all of it; then look where the pulse beats, and the two sides are after the ears, and they are both reopened; then sign the sides, then cover each with a sponge wet with 2 parts. until the cut comes up to the bone, and that is done by the large side of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, squeeze out the sponge from the artery and cover it on top; also cut it like 2 parts with a saw.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the pulse is covered, then let it go up continuously without stopping.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Et s'il le poignent à lor naissance, se li estraint les euls qu'il ne se muvent tant qu'il naissent.
de emigrainne	De migraine.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old migraine comes, and catarrh with moisture from tears and heat in the temples and old sore foreheads and similar things, and is medicine by the methods of medicine cure and all this does him no good, let we draw out the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, if com we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is that the patient makes a second hair on his temples, and hears to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not too tight except for some men who are too cold; and if it is re-tightened, then extract its neck from some sheets, then rub the place with no sharp cloth, and raise the place of warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulate where this is the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	And then peel the skin lightly until you come to the artery, and twist it up like pinches, and remove it well from the cloths that are soiled by each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it to the point of the hook, and cover it with that part according to the quantity of .ij. chapters. For if it is not covered, then neither will the blood go through all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And twist the blood of 30 chapters until 15; and if the artery is large, then you must bind it with 15 loops of a strong double silk thread, which will not be broken in front of the splashing of the wound, and will flow away from blood; then cut off the excess that is between the 15 loops at that same time, and then, if you see fit, so cauterize it with the cautery cutlass until the bone is reached while the hair is still cut; and this is the operation of the hot wound, if the patient does not have a fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is a great help for ending moisture; because this is even greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For when extracting arteries, you should fill the artery's place with fine cotton and put on well-made tents; and when you take them off, treat with dry medicines that cause a char to be born, and with tents, until they are healthy; and if there is no cupping by cautery, or you employ the place of vitriol and extract it by hand so that the blood is extracted; and if you do not have this present, put your thumb on the place as long as the blood is frozen, and raise the place of cold water as long as the blood stops flowing, and extract it in the way that should be; and the one that is moistened and lighter during the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this fire-trimming on both sides, but let the trimming be well spaced to last longer with heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too soft, its heat lasts less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two tools a space of an inch, and then when you have tied up the two ends, and you measure with the sharp edge on both sides until it comes to the bone, and cope the vein in the two ends; and they are separated by the two nails because it is not stiffened by this cautery everywhere; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes come out of veins that are on the forehead at the top of the skull, and there is no benefit from medicine that is done, and you see the face of the patient turn gray, and feel a cold movement like shivers; and if oil is held and wet so that the hairs of the eyebrows fall, and the eyebrows burn, and are scorched by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to do this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And it was called the 'old cure', and that is what you do to the patient who has hair on his forehead, then make .iij. cuts even with the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts should be as if .ij. doi all along the forehead up to the nose, and the other .ij. are made .ij. inches apart above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the .ij. jawbones, and each wound is three fingers wide;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and put an sponge and mowt of drapels on it to wipe out the blood, then bottle up the spatumil from  .ij. parts where this is the shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	As for the incision that is to be made from the temple to the second incision; and scrape off all the cur that is between the two cleavages up to the bone, and then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spike.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if it is placed in the first cleavage the instrument which is called 'chitellaire', and is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other is smooth, not sharpened, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And set the chisel-cutting towards the horse's back at the cur, and the chisel is smooth towards the bone, and the bottle as far as it comes to the middle cleavage. And scrape all the cur that descends from the head to the incision so that it is continuous until that which opens from the cur, and then do the same in the middle cleavage until the other one; and then remove it equally, and express the blood; then put into each cleavage a tent of fine cotton cloth, and put soaked drapes in wine and oil and vinegar, and keep so that the abscesses don't come; and on the third day unbind him, and impart a great quantity of cold water, and then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures for wounds, until he is well.
dou reume des eulz	And take off the cur
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When no venereal catarrh has been contracted by habit, and you see the hairs tenacious and small, and weakening of sight, and burned papers; and the hair falls out, and where it falls in pain ague comes to the patient, then know that these matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure which is there, if this is so, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you command the patient to rub his forehead, then make a large cut in the middle of the forehead, and another wide incision; commence from the left temple to the right temple, and cut down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the muscles that move when he drinks; and when the bone is exposed, if you suck all the blood out with a sponge, then bind it between the .ij. lips of the cut and put on some cotton wool and linen; then spread some wet drapelz over it (wraps), soaked in wine and oil, and take care not to touch an abscess; when it is exposed, if you rub the bone until it starts to grow, then cure with things that dry up, which cause char.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take .ij. parts of flower of wheat, and three parts of colophony, and make an ointment thereof; and administer it into these wounds to cause char all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stooping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All who have ears are of the four things: or grain, or beast, or small stone or similar thing such as iron; or seed, such as peas and beans; or flowing thing such as water and easily flowing and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it chings in the ear, whether a stone or any other thing that does not fit in the ear and does not enter it, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, then pour a little violet oil or oil of sesame, then do an extraction; and what is done is to shake with heat, and stop the nostrils when the shaking comes, and put strips of cloth or wool around the ear; and raise the ear above. Many times this cure works; and if it does not work, then extract it with a fine tweezers, from which this form comes:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, then extract it with a small double-ended needle; and if it does not come out with the needle, then make a thread of air and hold the head of the ear with it or a piercing instrument strongly, and stop what is inside the ear with soft wax so that it cannot enter with the thread; then try again, for many times this cure works; and if it does not work in any way, then take glut of milk, such as is used to make cheese, and put some cotton in it; then press the glut on the stone or whatever it is, and try again.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not come out with the methods described above, then split the ear in half as if splitting an apple, and spasms; and the way to split the ear so that you make a small cut at the base of the ear, following the shape of the ear, and then put the cut part between your hands and raise the ear above, and make a small cut in the root of the ear on the fat or liquid depending; and let the cut be as thin as a moon, until you find the stone, then hold it with your strength, and suck it gently into your mouth; and the cure until it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is seed corn that is infected and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then administer. i.e. a sputum of thin milk according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision on that grain. But do not make it when you think the grain is moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them carefully and finely with a pin and with a scissor, as we have said, so that the extractions are orderly.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	So that the patient uses sneezing of first condisi, and ample the ear with old cotton. And it is gisans on that ear or the aigre is. if it is, it is good. If not, take many small pieces according to the length of your finger toward and light, and heat them a little at the fire; and put one or another piece in his ear, and chop from another part, and make an incision on another piece on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop making this piece after piece until the aigre comes out all, and so it goes; and if you see it, take 1.i. junon, and bottle one of the chiefs in the ear, and the other chief take from the fire until the most dou jonc is burned; then make another again with others junons until the aigre comes out all, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the arrow, if it is a small one, like a bug or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is a big one that can be felt, then administer extraction by pinceures; and this is the lightest thing to be found in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you cannot cure them as we have said in the chapter on division and treatment of distillations, and if the cure is not effective, then look at the ear towards the sun; if there are no worms, take a fine pin and if they do not come out, hold the ear by its shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be tight below and wide above. And pour in the subtlest oil into the ear according to the quantity of the pain of the patient, then suck out the form completely; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not come out, split them between cotton as I have said in the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, administer distillations that the old ones have tried in the extraction of worms, and you will find them or treatment of distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, from which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or gold tight in a small hole, and above to distill; and for pressing inward the distillation with an instrument of bronze well made so that if you see a razor, and you put cotton around the tip forward; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the cain (cane), and the cain is in the ear; then pour into the razor all the cotton, and press your hand carefully so that the oil is distilled or the scent comes out of the ear; and smell the patient's medicine inside, and let the distillation be heated on the fire as it is distilled in the ear; and keep it from being too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the support of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by an injury from a splint [a piece of wood or metal used to support or hold something] inside the ear, or a cart falls into the ear, and this splint comes completely into the ear sometimes, so that one cannot see it; and there is no harm done to one, and they can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	So that which comes completely into the ear sometimes, so that one cannot see it, is of great benefit in many conditions, and in this you should put the ear of the sick in the sun; and look inside: if you see the operation apparent, if the work has done all this skin-care with which this is formed:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be careful and cut off in front and behind all plain, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the operation is a splint or a bar of the ear, if you hold it with subtle scratches, and break it lightly, until this splint is all broken.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the swelling is entirely in the ear, take a fine sharp razor and warm it slightly, then put it at the root of the ear. If you feel the swelling which the patient feels as grit in his ears, pierce lightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a small tent according to its width from the perforation, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not make any tent until the wound is healed, or take a small tent and soak it in rosewater, and powder it with vitriolic brooch; and if you see fluid running out of the ear, cover it so that you remove the tent and moisten another tent made of rosewater and wax, until the swelling comes out; then cure it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the discharge of blood comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that heal the discharge of blood which are or to treat with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the hair of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Take the hairs that come in sheets when they are moist and dry, so that you stretch them with tweezers and the comb of a spitail from their roots; then put on top of the place vitriolic broid.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not peeled off, then the fire cautery with the thin lens-shaped cautery, and the cautery afterwards after cutting out comes to rest; and many times they come back, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	from the grease
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in sheets things that seem grease in form and hardness, and for this it is called "grandine", and is a gathering of moisture thick on the paper above and below; the ovraiges are these: take care if the grandine mutates from one side to another, and this is a light thing to know; make the cut wide, then the scorch of each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and cover. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper, do not harm the patient; and if the split is large, so cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for the oilmens will soon restore it and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hair is falling out at the base towards the upper part of the ear, then flip the paper over and are the hairs to two pincers, and the cope and press on both sides; and if the paper is removed by the incision, it does no harm; and when the hair has been cut, let the oil of salt water be poured on, and cure the hole of that which causes so much pain until the patient is well.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	is produced when the paper is wrinkled above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears come out; and because they lie on their faces from then on, and sleep like that, and their cheeks are wet with the exinach which opens in the oil. And when you press the leech between your fingers, you feel the exirnach coming out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way to use it is that the patient puts his head in your lap; and then take a linen sheet, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exirnach contained in each part, and then put it on top of him; and press with your fingers from both sides so that the exirnach is assembled in the middle; and cut into the moisture with a sharp blade, making a slit of the right size for the wound made in the vein; and then close up the skin perfectly until you have brought out all the exirnach; and in several dispositions the exirnach comes from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then from all a piece of linen between your two palms at the end, and bring back your hand to the left and to the right until it is spread; and be careful not to jerk in the tear, lest you come to all the spittle up to the oil, lest you spill it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the head does not come out in the compression of the tear, then bring it lightly by half a finger so that it appears; then take it as we have said, then moisten the cloth with water and place it on its place, and strain from the bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if such men grind silk and put on it that moisture which is delayed. Then the doctor cures until he is well. And if he comes to the base of the appendix, the doctor applies poultices soothingly until he is well.

de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the porrittion comes in oil, there are 1j. ways: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or a cut, or a cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. And the method of treating this in the text is that you should split those bonds, and separate the lips of him, and put linen inside, and leave it until it heals; and you should not use anything in the cure of him that dries and constricts. For if you do this, the disease will come back worse than before; but if you use softening things, such as fenugreek; and water or ale or linseed seeds are cooked, and olive oil is melted in any of the oils, and wrap a tent around it, and cure him from that.

And the treasures of your cure that you take care not to change according to the form that it was before; and the works that we have said are only valid if they are applied from this disease, that it does not return according to the form that it was before.

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil

de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Miltimes the neck has a disease called "telul", and grows large and becomes very painful to look at; so you must cut it open at the beginning, and burn the bone, then put fire on it; if you delay doing this when it is large, it may get hard, be yellow in color, and not have any feeling: but do not touch it with iron because that is an abscess; for if you cut into it even once, great evil will come to the patient. The abscess should be touched very lightly, not by a yellow color, and you can see that it can all be covered, so the patient is empty and does not feel pain, and cure him with dry and restraining things.

des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A home, within the lips, appears a hard, grainy-like pustule, small and large; therefore, you should turn the lips, split each one at the tip, and catch it with pincers, and then apply the vitriolic paste to the area until the pus is drained; and then wash it off with water, and treat the area with dry things until they are healed.
de la char des gencives	the color of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Maitre de l'art de la chirurgie, il est bon d'apprendre que les dents qui ont été arrachées doivent être maintenues avec des tenailles, et la racine doit être coupée, et laisser couler le sang; puis mettre sur le trou du vitriole ou d'autres poudres qui retiennent l'humidité et séchent; et si celui-ci revient après l'incision, et arrive souvent, si la racine est coupée une deuxième fois, et cautérisée: s'il ne revient pas après la cautérisation; et voilà les formes des instruments pour combler.
des sordens	Orde de la chirurgie
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Orde de la chirurgie:
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	Orde de la chirurgie:
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Here is the translation of the text:
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not fall out, then take any of these tools and put it inside from all sides slightly, and move it as you did first. And if the gap is wide and deep, then fill it with gauze, and place the tweezers lightly on either side; and it is necessary to work carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must do well to avoid breaking it, and if a part remains, and return it to the patient by the malice of the root with greater pains than the first. And you must guard that you do not do so as does the ignorant patient who, because of his haste and pride, often breaks none but the carriage, and never attains to what we have told; but brings about none but great illness for the roots that he delays, or for the carriage that he breaks, as we have often intended; and when the tooth is drawn, if you wash the hole with wine or ale and salt; and they run away from it without stopping, so often comes a pain, if you employ the hole of vitriol broiled; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, so that the teeth do not break first, are long-tipped and thick-handled, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:

de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth

quant li dent lochent	When the tooth moves
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth moves, either by percussion or by chewing, and the patient cannot press upon what he chews because it makes him sneeze; and you have cured them with restricting medicines, and that does not work; then, you should restrain it with a gold thread, because silver thread turns green and spoils, but gold never does; and make the thread neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you notice any toothache, pick up the thread and double it between the two teeth, then place the caps between the teeth, if there are more than one, until you have reached the sound tooth on the other side; then, restart the wrapping gently and carefully, until it does not move; and if it dessticks, or the thread rubs, then tighten it with another thread; if it dessticks and stays in place, leave it tight, and let it stay as long as possible, and if it comes loose, or the thread rubs, then tighten it with another thread; if it stays in place for a long time, and works well, and that is the form of the teeth and the figure of the wrapping of the sound teeth and the caps of the two teeth, if you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is loose, if you set it in its place, time after time, as we have said; and do not meddle with it who are not skilled and chịu; and never make the shape of a tooth of an ox's bone, and set it in its place where it has failed, and hold it fast as we have said, and delay and endure for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To remove the copper from the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No one should take copper from the tongue or nature it out, except in an accident of sore throat; and the procedures are such that you open the mouth of the sick person and put your hand under his chin, and draw the tongue; then cut off the copper from the back with a large knife, as much as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or no pain, and it is the result of an accident of sore throat, then cut it off with a sharp edge, and guard that the incision is not too perfect, lest the artery be cut; and when you have done so, take away pure rose water and cold water, then put a bandage of linen on the tongue; and dye it every night, so that the root cannot come up. And if the sore comes back, then cauterize with a lenteen cauldron, which is good for this; then cure it with other remedies until it is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see red or black or hard color on it or not feel it, for this is a cancer; and if it inclines to blenchor and has moisture, then pour the copper in and make an incision with a fine scalpel, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the sick person comes to you, put it on vitriolic broth until it is well, then return to your procedure as much as you want; then take away the water of aise and seil, and cure it with other remedies until it is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch with iron for the pain of blood; but leave it until it dies, and then you will remove it, or it would break by itself; and if it is a white color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it up, but first see if the abscess is hot and has calmed down. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his neck be straight, and he opens his mouth and puts his elbows between his hands, and presses the tongue onto all the instrument, from which this form is made; and be of silver or fine gold as our knives:

Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess; and I had it very well closed all the way up, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was stopped up, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for 1 day or 2. And this abscess was so high that he had been 2 or 3 rains by the 2 or 3 openings where it was coming out. So I waited a while, and put in one of the onions, then pulled it hard, and cut off a large portion of bow; then put another in the other opening from which it was coming out, and pressed her mouth shut and her tongue; then I put the onion into these abscesses, and put some in, and there came out only a little bit of blood; and so the passage in her throat opened up for the woman, and she began to drink water and wine again, and did not stop cutting off this abscess for a long time; and the abscess went back, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it got very big; then I took hold of it and cauterized it inside her throat: so it stopped growing; and I left these parts, and there was nothing but God did after me.
de l’uve	about the grape vine
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.
