When it has been treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, and you see that the aposteme is calm, and thin, then you should cut it; and that which is round assembled and not far away; and it is bloody or of a reddish color or black, then you should avoid the incision. For there is great danger with this disease. Therefore, when you see it, according to the way I have said, that its blenchor and its longesce, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument we have mentioned above; then put the oncine into the eye, and turn it around, and cover it with .i.i instruments that I said in incising .i.i mandrels. And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; for if you do, it hurts the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of .i.i mandrels, and cure until it is healthy. And if the patient fears to be covered, then you should use an instrument for cauterization when the pain is painful. The way of cauterization is sharp. And it is that the patient put his head on your well, and then he presses his tongue to the instrument we have mentioned, where there is a sharp edge, so that it is not too thick or too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, from which this form comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put your hand on his head where the hair grows, so that he can let the medicine touch his eye, as if with a spoon, and place the instrument on all the medicine on the eye; and may the patient lie on his side, so that he salivates and his mouth water comes out of the medicine into his throat, so that it does not go down to his chest and burn him; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye for an hour's half, until you see it heal and the medicine has calmed its stings; and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument with all the cotton around the eye, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and wash it after 3 or 5 days. And if you need to clean the medicine out of the eye, if it has been put in, and after the cauterization rinse it with very cold water, and cure it with gargles until it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than the incision or cauterization; if it has been cured by smoking in this way, take calamus and yarrow and oregano and thyme and chamomile and hawthorn and other herbs, and put them all together or any of them in a 1-liter pot, and pour water into it easily, and bring it to a boil; and the pot should be very tightly covered with a strong lid, and set the pot on 1 instrument prepared in this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Et soit d'argent ou d'arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l'uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; après lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faiches ceu au comencement de l'avenement de l'aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que à la declination d'aposteme chaut. Et si cist estrument n'est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craffe d'uef, si que li bouche au malaide n'ait mie trop chaut; car li craffe d'uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c'est bone cure ensamble salut.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Muitas vezes se arde na garganta osso ou espinha de peixe, ou nenhuma coisa; então é conveniente que você tire o que você pode ver e pressione a língua ao sol com todo o instrumento, para que você possa ver o movimento da coisa; e o que não se abre para você e está encoberto na garganta, é conveniente que você faça vomitar o doente assim como a carne é cozida no estômago; talvez, se isso não funcionar, o doente engolirá um pedaço de esponja, ou uma peça de nável, ou uma raiz de alface, ou 1/4 de pão seco; e prenda a esponja com um fio e depois a transglutir; e quando ela chegar ao fundo, se abrirá, então puxe forte; e se ela não vier forte de tudo o que dissemos, pegue 1/4 de instrumento de mergulho de acordo com esta forma:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	E seja o instrumento curvado na testa se ele puder entrar com mais facilidade na garganta e levantar a cabeça para cima; e tenha cuidado para não tocar a epiglote, de modo que ela não caia; e mova vale que o doente boğa o instrumento, para que ele faça vômito ou seja encoberto; se ele engolir, ou ele vomitar todo o instrumento uniformemente, até que ele saia.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No time is medicine for the blood, if as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not profit, then look at the throat of the patient under the sun, so that you press it with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the blood, take a fine hook, or tiny tweezers that are worth to him. And if he is not worth, then take a piece of hair from a horse, and pour it into the throat of the patient, then pour the hair  .i. hot, and do this often. And if the patient is dark all day, then take a full pint of cold water, and open the mouth, and drink it down, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the blood feels the water, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not spit as we have said, then submerge the patient in ash water, at the instrument that I have told you in the smoke of the oven; do this often, for it will not gag. And the way of the smoke is that you press a pot or it has viscous charcoal, and let the cover be torn so that it falls into the middle, and on that hole is the head of the instrument; then pour your smoke, and the patient put the end of the pipe in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes to the blood; and the blood will now come out, and if it does not come out, then begin the smoke again by many times; and make the patient thirsty, and drink salty things and bitter, and do not drink water; and then the proper work is that she goes away by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument to see if one can tell, is, when one can see it, similar to hooks twisted for entering into the throat; and has the appearance of a doctor's pick, and has sharpness of lime, so that whoever takes it cannot leave it; and see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the ointment for abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The head of an abscess has two forms, one that is moist and the other that is dry. The moist one comes from the middle of the head, and the dry one comes from the jaw. And each has its own nature in work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If an abscess does not need to be pierced, then let it dry out as long as the swelling lasts; and if one is crut, then pierce it when the swelling has subsided, so that it will not hurt the main member. For if an abscess comes from a joint, and you leave it until it is rotten inside, perhaps the ligature and nerve of the joint will be damaged, and this causes contraction in that limb. But if an abscess comes from the principal member, then let it heal; and if one is crut, then pierce it before it has healed completely, so that the one that comes from the foundation does not rot to the end, and become a fistula, and cannot be cured well.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you know the time for piercing an abscess that is dead according to its completion, and that is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the stirring up of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where there is most thickening of the skin, and where it opens most easily; and let the perforation be made with a long knife, and if it is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves, and in all the limbs evenly, where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that are swollen, according to the limb. And when abscesses are in the flesh, so as they must burst, you leave the piercing until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them before this, if you draw along the course of his blood, and it is full of filth; and perhaps harden the lips and deepens him. And if there is an abscess that has pierced according to the largeness of the limb, according to what the members require. It is necessary that you bring small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many splits according to the appearance of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover them up, and to plug; when they have been made as 2. i. drapels, and are softened, it is necessary to do so as one does with buboes: and if there are such that are split in 3. angles, and if there are such whose lips are also split like the skin of mirth, as abscesses of the angles; and if there are such that are made into a round size, and other sizes and a similar appearance of being cut.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those that are swollen, according to the limb. And when abscesses are in the flesh, so as they must burst, you leave the piercing until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them before this, if you draw along the course of his blood, and it is full of filth; and perhaps harden the lips and deepens him. And if there is an abscess that has pierced according to the largeness of the limb, according to what the members require. It is necessary that you bring small abscesses, small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many splits according to the appearance of the greatness of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover them up, and to plug; when they have been made as 2. i. drapels, and are softened, it is necessary to do so as one does with buboes: and if there are such that are split in 3. angles, and if there are such whose lips are also split like the skin of mirth, as abscesses of the angles; and if there are such that are made into a round size, and other sizes and a similar appearance of being cut.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the discharge from the wound comes out, you put cold water and quickly, and wet 2. i. drapels, and place them over the wound many times. And if the discharge persists, you put government and medicine, and the powders that I have said in your hands in this book, and if it is or not dry, and the leavings of the wound are very nervous, it is necessary that you put on tents and drapels wet in wine and oil warm; and if it is dry, and the leavings are meaty, you put on drapels wet in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said; and then take off the abscess and clean it and cure it, as it should be, until it is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this everywhere in the treatment of abscesses: but I have told you how one must go before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the ointment.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Here is the translation of the first paragraph:
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Here is the translation of the second paragraph:
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times there is an abscess at the throat, and they open the arteries and veins, and they come from one place to another, and they are swollen and inflamed; and each scrofula is properly within its rib, as the nut and the abscess of the neck, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that do not want to obey health. Now, therefore, when you see one that is of a good disposition in the breast, and has a color like that of the flesh, and is silent on both sides, and is not deep; it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape each part, and there are  .ij. lips of the heart to be tied with one thread, if you need it, as we have said in the neck abscesses; and trim little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor let the blade slip, lest you do harm, and look too far ahead, lest you cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	If you cut the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to work, then put vitriolic acid on it, or some powders that restrain blood, and squeeze the wound; and leave the wound until the abscess is calm, and the wound is softened, and begin to rot. And when the scrofula has hardened at its root, if there are no small scrophulas, cut them and clean them. And if there is a big scrofula at the root of the neck, it is not necessary that you cut that scrofula in its root, but bind it with a double strong thread, and let it hang by it, without causing any harm; then employ cotton dipped in unguent to dress the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you cut the whole scrofula, you must assemble the .ij. lips of the wound and sew them now, without causing any delay for the size of the scrofula; it is necessary that you bind its root, and pull hard, and sew it as we have said. Those scrophulas that hold superfluity, pierce where it opens; and pierce in this way, following the order of the one before, then introduce tentes with unguent and similar things, so that it corrupts whoever is delayed by corruption; and when the wound has been well cleaned, if it is healthy, then dress it with unguent, covering with a cloth, as long as it remains healthy.
de squinance	Here is the translation of the text:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke and wrote about the lancing of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the script from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the slicing of the throat, which is called the epiglottis, be removed; and no aid should be sought from anyone, for all the veins and the pulse of the patient are in the mouth or the throat or.ij. mandres.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the canal of the pulse, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis so that the stranglehold from which there is no escape does not come.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we do so with a sharp blade.iiij circles or a small slit through which the quantity of the cut does not reach the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if they are suitable for cutting the epiglottis that there is no chip, and the vase is long of it;
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entire length, then cuts the cartilage as far as it comes to the chin; and avoid cutting the windpipe, unless you see something, and then cut the syfac, as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that jumps out by the place that has been broken, and by the loss of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts strangulation, join the .ii. lips of the wound together, and the whole skin below the cartilage; then administer medicines that make blood flow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one must not do this as long as the throat is entirely closed up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the lack of it brings him back to life.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	And then cover the epiglottis so that the patient cannot die, and he breathes through the wound, and in this way he is preserved from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and so the elder instructs that the wound be kept open as long as the evil of the disease has not passed, and it has passed in iij days or iiij
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded that the wound be sewn and healed, until it was cured;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw;
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a knife, and put it in her throat, and went out through the monestary door;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called by the healer, and I found it just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that it had discharged; I saw that it had not broken a vein but had come from deeper inside the body, and the blood had flowed out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried to bandage the wound, healing it until it was cured;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the damsel only became red-faced, and afterwards she returned to her usual self;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	for I do not know if there is fear in the surgery of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	is called "gorge hernia", and is a great hernia in the color of a yellow, and is very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it is according to .ij. manners: natural, and accidental; or natural has no gadgetry.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accident happens according to .ij. manners, one is resembling grass on us, and another manner is resembling an abscess coming from us of arteries;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is doubt, and it does not come to operate fire furiously that in the one who is small, and prove and search all the intruder:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you prove it as well as grass our, and can not at all, if the cup, if it cups us, and tries to all his beard, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well altogether, and treat if necessary, so that it is completely healthy.
des nous	of the fire cautery
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways to perform this treatment, all of which I will describe.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and so it is necessary that I make the full distinction between our methods and those of others.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that the treatment is hot and fiery, until the fever and chills have passed, and then the purifying is complete; afterwards, the fever and chills subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With this nut there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains 1 [unit of measurement] syrup, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the skin, and begins also like a kernel, and becomes thick.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to their appearances, or fat, or moist, and all of their colors are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the cure of the nut, you should try and ask first about the instrument that is called "entremissoire", according to its form or the paste that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the way of the investigation of abscesses is that you squeeze or more moistly place your fingers in the abscess, and turn them little by little, until you feel that the instrument has penetrated the pus, then do it according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the instrument of insertion, and take care not to break it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture runs quickly, that it be colored, so that you do it like I said with other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the instrument of insertion no moisture comes, know that it is greasy, so you do it in a cross-wise way, and take hold of it with tongs, and scorch it lightly on each side, and leave it at rest where it lies, so that you get it healthy with the not;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot get it out healthy, take it apart piece by piece so that nothing remains still;
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if I don't stay, he returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it takes a little time, and there is no pain, but employs the wound with some corrosive water, and removes the wound, and puts on things that calm the abscess, and cures other things until it is well;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if we take a great deal of it, so that the .ij. lips of the wound are cut off, and he cures what causes it to happen;
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound is opposite or other if you hurry and employ the place of vitriole broiet, and leave it ii days or iii, as long as the wound leaks, and returns to copper what has been left;
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here is the translation of the text:
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles used for piercing sorceresses, and they are of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and they move easily those that are yellow, and are more proven to pierce black lead in order to encircle the corbales of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of the instruments are of various shapes, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are instruments that have three quarters of three manners as well;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if one has three combs and are also of three types; and if one has two combs and one comb only, and are of three types; and all of them are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these to that one does is sharp, and such ones have I who do not cut well but only from one side, because one scours the skin so as not to hurt the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these interpositionals are the alambics set in many parts, so that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of three types: great, small, and moderate, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and don't use more than one pair of shoes that are not worn out, because they are like legs, arms, nipples, elbows, and similar things;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never make another small instrument that resembles the shape of a scraper, according to this form, so that you do not hurt yourself with it:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and never place it in the place that hurts when rubbing together, and never rub according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	and never inflate the breasts of certain men when they tighten them, because they look like a woman's breasts:
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain lame and swelled up, and who must be cured if it goes according to this form from this line: b. until: .
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and employ the wound with medicine, encasing it, then stitch together the iij lips of the wound, and cure as long as it is healthy;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and let it suck in the milk, and be softened by its size so as to resemble women's breasts, if they are made into iij knots above, by iij similar cleavages;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	of which the larger line is held to the smaller one at its end, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this form, from this line .b. until the line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then peel the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and give those that we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure until it is well.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not well, or the incision is not entirely made, so that the patient does not rest, or for the evacuation of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton wet in a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until the juice and the remaining fat have evaporated, then treat it until it is well.
des apostemes des asselles	the heels of the feet
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	The cysts that come from abscesses are handled like hard scrofula or if they have ribs and contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture are to be cut according to this form, from the line B up to the line G. :
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels that are in the abscess are empty, if you employ cotton wool and leave it there for another day, then remove all the wool, and treat with an ointment appropriate to this until it is healthy again.:
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then cut it as we have said in the treatment of scrofula, and if the wound is oozing, apply fire cautery as we have described.:
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the flesh above it is tightened, then many abscesses and also the escape of blood come about and an abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows how to recognize when it is for the artery, then the abscess will be long enough to heal completely.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it on both sides, if you feel a twisting sensation; and when it is for the vein, if it feels like it is being pulled apart.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and this is crazy to cut this abscess, and most when it is dislocated at the ankle and at the knee and elsewhere, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore the treatment of iron must be avoided, and that which is at the shoulder must also be avoided, and in that which is swollen with an artery, cut through the skin above it longwise;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate on the waist as one does, and carefully separate the artery from the tissue, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert an awl, and drive it through just to the other side of the coast, and pull the artery with a double thread of silk, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples;
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then point out the place which is between the 17th ties of an intramossoire while the sun does not go out who is there, and let it be free the aposteme;
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then provide the cure that causes fever, as long as the line trembles;
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then treat this with ointment coming from here, as long as it is healthy;
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the aposteme is by the size of the vein, then you have to have it in your hand what you can get from the aposteme all over the leather,
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	Then put the needle through the hole that you hold in your hand, and let it have .i. a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	Then tie the apothecary, as I have told you, or one of the two ends to the thread;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, then put another needle on all of the apothecary to the incision of the first needle, and pull out the threads in three lengths;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cut off the surplus of the apothecary, then cut off the surplus of the curl and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then pour over it with a damp cloth in wine and oil, then bring the cure of tent and ointments as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	of the abscesses of the nuts
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, when the abscesses come in the artery and the vein, they come to the nuts when it is wounded, or by too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens in the shoulders and the arms and in all joints, and its color seems like the color of the heart, and it is in many dispositions without pain;
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when they are held in place, if the patient feels pain, and it is not fully healed, but take care of it.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and do not move well on all sides, and do not go forward or backward, and do not cover with iron; perhaps there will be a contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the head or in front, make the skin with a spatule.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the aphesis is small, if it has nails, and cut it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, if the hangnail has come off with the skin, then burn it, and then cut it, and sew up the wound, and let it heal until it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	big holes hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	No time has come to the belly and no other part of the body, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its appearance, and is the subtle root, and the big tree; and there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw. I. home who had .ij. or bellies that were more similar to mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and they were broken open, and they ran together with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found one to be XVIII ounces in weight, and the other XVII Z. and that their incision was such that if you look at it, the patient is wet, and the color of the artemisia is bleached and moist and has a fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the cut is with a wide scalpel, and the fire cautery is ready in your presence. For often there are too great irregularities of blood, and he comes to you without delay, so hasten then to cauterize;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient sweating and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made piece of flannel, and bind it to the artemisia as we have said, and leave it for II days;

Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess that has become infected, and I will come to the treatment of leprosy hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the bad blood
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	as a bad smell that comes from cauterizing a wound or a fracture of the skull, and it is on the belly and there are some of the bad smells, so as it happens in other wounds, or from blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind;

puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then instructs him to cut softly between your hands,

puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	And make half of the abscess at the top to all the great hook.

dou chancre	and for the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	and for the ulcer We have spoken in the division about the appearance of ulcer, and how it should be operated upon with medicines, and how one should cauterize the wound; and we say that an ulcer is incurable when it is in the face or in the genitals, and great care must be taken in its treatment, and the ancient book says that when an ulcer is in a good position to be cut, like an ulcer in the breast or in the loins, or in any other part where it can be easily reached; and when it is large and old, then one should only approach it, for I have never known anyone to cure it, nor has anyone ever cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the incisions, when they are in a good position to be cut, as we have said, is that you never purge any black bile; then make it well if it has manifest repletion, then afain make it well  .i. a good place for the incision; then put on your oncins or ulcer, and shave all around it, and burn all around it without leaving anything; and let the blood run freely, and press firmly with your hand or with anything, and if the bleeding stops, cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then heal it with another remedy until it is well.
de ydropisie	from dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	from dropsy
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the idropisia is going into the intestines: it is fitting that you should split it open on both sides of the navel, right at the top of the hand; and if the idropisia is caused by liver disease, then your split should be on the left side of the navel; and if it is caused by bile, then it should be on the right, and it is only fitting that the patient should lie on his back on the split, so that the excess does not run to that weak part.

And on one side there is 1 hole, and on the other 2 holes, and on the other 1; and the head is cut so as to look like a quill, and this is the form of the incision that the authors cut the quill with:

fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. And when it urines, if it is not tied, let it urinate, and then put it back; and perhaps he will not have any trouble, because the urine that comes strongly does not leave the foreskin closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. des pustules de la verge	of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	come often come pus in the penis, and it is an ugly appearance; and there are both evil and not evil ones; so that you should squeeze them with one hundredth of a drop of egg white, and clean them all over, then put cotton wet with egg-yolk extract on it; then cure it with the extract until it is well.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. And if the pus is evil in color and foul-smelling, then you should apply fire to it. For when you cure it all together, if it is not firmly set in the foreskin, then it will come out black and corrupt in its foreskin and where the cocoon is; so you should burn all of it that is black and corrupt, then put it on a plaster of honey and flour which has been made from the bark of pomegranates and dates, then cure it with other cures until it is well.

And if it is a very difficult case to deal with, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a spatulum on the top of the penis and the skin; then carefully remove between 21 and 25, and put a thin cloth of linen wet in cold water, so that it does not burn again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	is not dislocated by continuing if it is like the other wounds; however, when we perform this operation of our own will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do it with the best work and the lightest hand for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old people did not say anything about circumcising their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greatest part of the masters and the most honorable who did circumcision at Dalar, and in strength, and in all a novelness; so it was because there are 1.2 threads, and by chance if one copes on that above and demore that dislocation.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovient copes, and is the pain double, and to the washing which is of Dalar is not assured the point of the member; and by chance escapes the nail the iron, and corrects the work, and often are born so that there is no need of washing and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	For the washing which is done in strength to all the thread of file I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the strengths cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Car when you press your hand, so that the fingers are equally shortened; but let the string be well-fixed around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think that you only bind the string around the penis with so much force, and then cause it to suffer in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then hold the string tightly between your hands straight, and stretch the forces between your hands so that the child cannot see them, nor any of the instruments; then place your hand on the penis and squeeze or rub, and turn it upwards as far as the head of the penis is in; then clean it well with the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the joint with a double string, then tie another string to it; and hold it between the two strings at the second ligature to the scrotum and little finger, and tighten the ligature between the two strings, then lift the penis up carefully and turn the head of the penis.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let it run a little and a little, for it is the wettest; and put powder on top of the powder and over the powder  .i. drapelet is glued with a mixture of baked egg white mixed with rosewater, confited with good oil and fresh herbs, and left alone until the next day, and the cure is cured as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces in the cleaning is this: the two fingers are to be spread and cut, and are the same as long as they are evenly shortened.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of cleansing if it is when the curets run out at the incision; so that you must extend it to your nail, as if the leans make an abscess; and let it dry evenly; and if you cannot hold it on your nail, then hold it with pliers, and then let it dry.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it has passed three days, and what is at the root of the penis is swollen, if you leave it until the pustule has been cleansed, and the skin has been peeled lightly; if you can move it easily, and keep away from the part of the penis, that will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the powder of bitter things over sore places, which we have said in the treatment of powders, and if you cope too much, and it goes up, that will not harm him; cure it then, as we have said, until it is well.
dou retenement de l’urine	double retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retained urine is due to a stone in the kidney, or frozen blood, or a bowel obstruction, or chafing from riding in a carriage, or similar things, which we have mentioned in the chapter on urinary retention.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine does not flow, and you see the retention due to a stone at the base or neck of the bladder, then let the patient lie on his back; and let them put pressure on their back, and extend their stomach from above their back, and restrain the patient so that they can lie as much as possible; and then force the base of the bladder to express the stone above, so that the urine flows.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If this does not work, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must use all the instruments that are called 'syringes', which have the following form: and let it be very light silver, as the feathers of an owl; and let the cannula be a palm long and half, and very fine at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the way to express the urine is that you take a double thread of silk, and tie it at the tip with wool or cotton, and pour the tip of the thread into the syringe; and drain off the excess of the wool and pour it into the syringe, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and a little cumin, and make the patient sit up, and moisten the bladder and urethra with oil of olive and water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then hold up the syringe lightly in the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the buttocks; then pour the syringe before the bladder, and let the urine flow into the thing that is empty, and this is not done according to this order but only because the person who leads him or she goes there twisted; then tie the thread all around the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it firmly, and make the urine run.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and start again with the syringe as long as the bladder is empty, and the patient remains calm.
des maladies de la vessie	for diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or sores come to the bladder, or rust is formed there, and you pour there water and medicines, if done with all the instrument that is called "clepsydra", and it is in this form:

et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle enema by which the bladder is enema: if it is here:

de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken about the division of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between the stone in the lower parts and all other signs; and how one must work when it comes to the bladder and the womb; and I will tell you openly and briefly about that.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is in the bladder often occurs in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder like water in its subtleness; and it opens easily, and rubs the patient's womb, and scratches it many times, and then becomes smooth; and it is light to recover the health of the children until they are 24 years old, and heavy for the elderly, and moderate for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have great stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to clean the patient with a hot poultice so as to extract all the pus that is in the intestines. For he never seeks the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and move them up to the chest so that the stone comes out of the bladder completely; then do not let it rest on its own; then make it sit between your hands, and remove the clothes from his legs, so that the bladder hangs down towards the ground; then examine and touch it.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut above the stone. And if it doesn't come out with touch, then moisten your right index with oil from your left hand, since the patient is old and mature; then pour it on its base, and examine the stone, and when you feel it with your two fingers, so that the water goes to the neck of the bladder; then press with your two fingers, and pour it out at the end where you felt the cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder in his hand, and command him to stretch with his right hand the anus up above, and with his left hand hold the skin that is beyond the anus in the part where one cuts; then pour the liquid, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make a notch between the pubis and the pelvis, not in the middle but at the cost of the left leg; and let it be right on top of the stone, and your two legs should be close together or against the pelvis, and the size of the traver should be wide from the outside, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	In case the press should fall away from the foundation, so that it does not work; and know that there is a part of stone where it has angles and edges: this is bad for extraction; and if there is a part which is round like a globe, resembling a ball and a circle, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	On the other hand, if there is a part where there are angles and edges, make the size larger; and if it does not fall, so that you can extract it with pliers which are like a file at the end, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you should use a sharp knife, cutting into it; and if you cannot grasp it like this, then open a small hole, and if it is broken, so that the extraction of vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, first bottle the largest one into the neck of the bladder, then cope it up, then cut it off, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are any. And if it is very large, so that it should be made to come out, and make a larger wound; for 10 things happen to the patient: or he dies, or his urine comes out suddenly by the way that the leach does not hold; but nevertheless you force him to extract him, or with pliers, as long as you extract him in pieces.

Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be it in three angles,
