de la piere des femmes	of the woman's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	May a stone be found in women, and if it is not found, there is great difficulty: the first is that the woman may be a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who can go to the physician's house, even though she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that one cannot find a well-informed woman in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the woman' stone is more perfectly formed than the man' stone, so that one must make a deeper cut, and there is great fear with it.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, send for a midwife who is well-informed, and if you do not find it, ask no more. et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if it does not come out, and this is the artery that is torn, then sprinkle the powder on top and squeeze out blood and pus, and do not repeat this, and leave the stone and do not extract it, because by chance the patient may die; then treat the wound.

de hernie carnouse	of hernias that cause pain
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	is made from water or white milk that is mixed with the seeds of fennel, which contains the essence of the onion; and is called "syfac", and never properly in the tapestry of the onion itself, if one believes that it is another type of onion; and this milk of the fennel between the white milk we have spoken of; and this one does not come out.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the procreation of this ramose thing is so of weakness that comes to coions, and is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And so often comes of percussion on the coions, and this moisture so many colors: or it is color declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous whites, and such happens more;

dou chastrement	of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Saiches that chastisement is prescribed in our law, and for this reason I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary to speak of it only in two ways: one is that the horse should answer when questioned about its own cure; and the other is that, since we often have needed to chastise certain animals for our aid, such as sheep, goats, and dogs and others. Therefore I say that chastisement is done according to these two ways: either by attraction, or by cutting. In the one that we do by attraction, we make the horse sit in warm water until its joints are softened; then grasp them with your hand until they have recovered and you no longer feel them. From the taunting of the size: it is necessary that you tan the animal, and press the leather of its joints to your left hand, then tie the suspension, and cut each hoof one at a time when you have well dried them; and do not leave any pot of strong medicine and subtle medicine that is over the hoofs; and this way of chastisement is milder than the one done by attraction, because it may happen that something of the joints is lost in the latter, through which the animal desires lust; then heal the wound until it has healed.

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb had dead babies, then another咨询 on that one, and rejected the death of the others.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called in to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I couldn't close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong poultice, and it took some time, then another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much at this, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.

et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and waited for the woman to be a little longer, and there was a little bow in place;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I have written this chapter on the ointment except for one thing, that when the master sees a strange thing, he may know how to help.

Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second is held back at birth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to keep her hair in place, and then make her sneeze with a pinch, and hold her hands away from her mouth and nose; and si tu veu l’assaincre avant qu’il naisse, il est necessaire que tu mandes au malaide qu’il leure de sa mere par ses nages, et puis tu le feras s’assaincre par ton aise.
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if he cries because of the pain, it is good. de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet felt the foundation pierced, but it has been stopped by a subtle medicine.

des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	are according to its manner: they are inside the fundament, also like grain of resin, and have small and large ones, and cut them at an angle.

Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you bring the suture together in this way: take a .i. twisted thread, and put it into a needle, and then wind the thread around the top of the needle, and pierce the needle from the other side, and twist the .ij. ends of the thread through the needle,
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is wide; and tighten the thread, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same to all of them, and leave 1 to stop the blood flow;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation .i. cloth moistened with oil or wax, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest until it has healed, and when it is healed, if they treat with ointment and other treatment, as long as it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Do not cut off the hair at the root.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times the hair falls out at the roots, and by nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you rub the point of a spitball or your nail on your fingernail, which does not let it get moist;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	and treat him as long as he is sore, as it fits.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if he cannot be made well, then begin to shave again more strongly than before, until the skin has healed and is burnt.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat him as long as he is well.
dou fremit	and the pain will go away.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Fingers are a small appearance in front of the body, and they grow very well.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And never does the vein burst, and one feels it as if dead, and it spreads throughout the whole body, and more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an owl or a strong vulture, and place that feather on the wound, until it turns purple all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand over the feather completely until you have covered the entire wound, and seal it completely, and rub the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make it of iron or brass according to this shape, and be subtle in size and run on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	and do not pierce it, so that you keep it in two, and press it; And if you see, so cauterize the pain, as it is before or with fire-cauterizing:
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the blister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one should make a blister of silver or brass, or of melted lead or quicksilver; nor should you make these small and large instruments according to the needs of those who will use them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These children, then, who are weak and suffer pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the catheter is small and great it is over wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and I have an opening or the belly is tied, so that you see it, and the chest is pierced through one side, and on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly or I put the medicine of a bottle of wine or parchment, and is pierced all around small openings,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each hole there should be a space, then pour into these holes a strong thread of twisted wire in 10 or in winding it around, and join the abdomen as if it were a goat;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, so that the instrument lies in front of a strong thread, then cauterize; and it is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil or olive oil or some other substance is applied to the head of the cauterizer, then pour it lightly:
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	and then the minister applies the cauterizer to his both hands together until it is completely filled, and then removes the cauterizer, and places the patient's legs against the wall,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps all night, then it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize him with the disease of decay in the belly, and the medicine is hastened to come out, if it is repeated as long as he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are in the fundament or abscess, so the cauterization is as subtle as for a child;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the subtle cauterization where the skin is tightened:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken above of the treatment of wounds; now we will speak of the treatment of hands and medicines, according to the process.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are, and according to the places where they are made, and for this reason they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things for which wounds are made are by the striking of a stone, or the height of a spear or a knife, or a lance or a staff or a sword, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Here is the translation of the text line by line into English:
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	"Here are the directions for treating various wounds according to the sections of the text:
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	"I say that when a simple wound appears on the head, and the bone is not broken, if it is from falling from a height or from similar causes, and the skin is partly torn and the wound is large:  "
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt slightly about the abscess: if it is little blood from the wound that comes to the head, and the blood goes in the opposite direction of the part that has been pricked;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and let the patient abstain from wine and meaty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not drink, if his meat is diminished, and he drinks no wine, neither does he eat cheese;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, cotton wetted with oil or wine of stinging;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess, if it is put on the wound, if it is fresh in all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will say a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the fire has moved it, if it is put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tenderness, if they are brought together by sewing, as I will say for wounds from the belly, from the sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it stands out, and it holds only a little, then cure the wound with medicine, and restore it with hard leather instead of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the patient to eat large meats, as tested and baked wheat, also like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or burn rust, and it has not reached the bone, then chop off all of it, and throw it away, and then cure it;
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has an artery in the wound or vein, from which blood cannot be stopped by medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find a dislocation, like the thread of a rope;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put this powder into them so that it hardens in such a way that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of this powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood 3 parts; live coal 2 parts, and the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and hold it firm, until it is well healed and has joined together all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it undissolved, if it swells; for the medicine should not be applied until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And one should not do any castor oil, when one does not have the incense or the dragon's blood, but that the arm has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arm has moved the wound, surely it is infected, even if one does not put any of this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some distilled water, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it heals.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with other remedies until it is well.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with very small tweezers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you after this about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the throat
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound in the throat and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the artery at the throat is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is a newborn, if there is no other device but to leave the healing, and do not put any restraint, for it hurts the newborns and makes them retreat.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not place on the wound anything is cold, for the substance of the newborns is cold, and their flow is with the skull, which is the most high limb;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be made, if like hot water in soft water, and mixed with oil of roses, and washed too in soft water;
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mineral according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then the cure until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and the wound is full of bowels, if it pierces or goes deeper;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if the artery is cut, and blood loss occurs, if it becomes dark, and the blood stops, and the cauterization is done properly;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the throat is cut, or if it bleeds, and the direction is kept, so that the meat does not spoil;
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If cautery is applied to the chin of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then slowly remove it, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with herbs until it is healthy again;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if there has been an impression of the bone, then apply pressure to it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, then if you can't hold them fast, and those that you cannot hold fast, leave until the wound has pus;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let the discharge be kept under control;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	if the wound is fresh, sprinkle the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as described in my chapter on the powder.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a sword or an axe
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a lance or sword, and the wound is deep, then observe the patient’s breathing: for thus you shall know that the wound is deadly.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh in all its strength, then put the powder on him at first hour, nor bind him with bandages so that he does not die completely.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to bed, and let the patient rest.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on a wound dressing, and bind it three times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no wound, put wet cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient lie on the wound 1 . i . jurs, or 1 . iiij., or more times;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, no bad trembling of the heart or strange movements;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good conditions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat the ulcers of tents and other cures as long as he is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot be healed, and operate, then know that there are fistulas; so heal it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is an incision with a blade or knife, and it is simple, or deep or on the back, then heal what is before;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, of stitching; and if it is small, of powder, and if it has broken into the bone, and has caused pieces to come off, then heal the wound, and the deep wounds if they are not healed;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not removed, let the wound run its course, and the extractions are uniform.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds and other limbs the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	double rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The double rupture of the abdomen is great, middle, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound, no less often than the intestines, or where the intestines are located, so that there is no intrusion of water;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitch is more difficult and no less painful than the small wound rather than the large one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	For this reason we do not put back the intestines, unless it is hot, and we do not put them back from cold to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	for the intestines swell sometimes so that they feel the cold, so let us put them back more often;
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because this causes the internal wound, because it keeps the intestines in their place while others...18.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the abdomen is according to three ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common stitches in the abdominal stitch have...
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitches of other wounds on the chest and other common private stitches are common to...
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and all the ways they are more proper with the stitch of the belly, and I will say each one and I will declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and there is nothing of the intestine out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and good thing is of the remedy, this is by one of the two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or for the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	For where the intestines are swollen because of the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, heat it in this way:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	moisten a sponge or .i. damp rag barely wet with cold water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in cold milk and garlic and spice,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine as long as the swelling is open;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never stops doing this restraining, and becomes soft that it is empty for deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling disappear, if you moisten the intestine with water or salt and cook it well,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by this it is stiffened at little of something;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument that is used to cut hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to let it bleed.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we do not chop off unless there is great necessity;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for splitting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	If you cut yourself in a corbeau, don't run away, and look at the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have broken out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it according to the natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you can do so, for this is a difficult thing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide, and is in the part of the loins below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	if you make the patient lie on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place their legs higher than their head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and is in the part of the loins below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if the head and breast are higher than the shoulder parts
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if a rupture from the belly is in the lower of the .ij. parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you find that the part that is torn is higher than the other part;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus one should treat what I say here for great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Here is a translation of the text line by line:
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	and then place your hand over it. Let the minister with the knife come to your aid who will pierce all the wound from side to side with his knife,

qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	who is desoz the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and put together the .ij. chief with the .iiij. together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	and pull out a double thread through the needle from both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and then put together the  .ij. heads of the wound in front of,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave  1.2 inches of space between, and then put another needle,
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	and then cut the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this according to what you need with the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is closed up;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and the needles are small and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	For the fine needles pierce all the ship, and the too large ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for so it comes that they are little.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and does not come to put the needles too far from the side of the ship and the hide.
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	that they pierce and open the wound in front of the stitch
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the heads of the needles, so they do not prick the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put tents or drapes on the heads of the needles to keep them from moving,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of sewing the needles is more convenient for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for he had suffered a needle or .ij.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and is that you join together the .ij. stitches of the leather and the .ij. stitches of the medicine with a sharp needle or he has a .i. strong thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these stitches all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	If I return the needle to the part where you have begun, in the way that one sews thread.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller thread;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch is made by the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew an opening that has been made or a wound,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded with a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in length,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and there were well over two palm's width of intestines,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was on his abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I took out the intestine then it had been  .xxiiij. hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and was sewed up just after .xv. days, and I treated it, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the miracle was that the mirror had been broken, and yet he lived.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where one cannot find it, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and put on more cotton wool 11 times a day, and wash with honey water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the 11 proper ways to stitch:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and thread it from the outside of the wound inward.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the skin on the right side, if you have sewn or stitched where you pierced with the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and pierce it from another side from within to where it is far.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and understand this stitch that you also sew like the skin-peeler does with the fur,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the medicine on one side and reapply it on the other, until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of stitching, which Galen explains properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is like any other fountain, which unites the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the main drugs to another in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	file an awl or tip of mirach near, and pierce that one only,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two parts of the syrup;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part all the way to the inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as a doctor.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce the other one from outside part all the way to inside, in two more chiés with needle that are on other side of the body;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the method of suturing and it is most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galens says so of this word, and no one testifies against it.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One should sew the belly with .ij. needles or thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one should put the needle from one side and the other, in the manner of those who sew with corroded needles.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the tear is in the middle of the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If the stitch is more painful than other stitches from the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound if they are such as the judgments of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that the fire has moved it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	If the intestine is pushed back and the cut is made, then put the powder on and cover it up,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if it moves again, place it on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the cord, and let the sutures and mirrors be;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as you would any other, until it is well.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, place cotton wool on it, as soon as it begins to come off,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and shake it .ij. times a day as long as it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need any other medicine in most cases where the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if you wet another light member in hot oil, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and set the arms, and stretch out the legs;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	If he feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and often happens
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if the black wine enemas are used, and sometimes putridity comes up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierces it, and knows that when it is the large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestinal tract called "jejunum" cannot heal once it has been torn.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	is due to the presence of veins and the subtlety of the entire body, as well as the nearness of its essence to that of the young.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound heals quickly, then it is like the intestine, while it is fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it becomes dark and putrid, so that you can see the black spot that causes it to rot, then
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	For there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	and then cut who is between the line,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place the two shoulders hanging from the part of the wound until far away so as to facilitate the extraction when the zephyr blows, and the wound swells.
de la routure dou boueil	from the cut on the brow
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	For I have seen some honor that a noble man or a warrior's belly was pierced by a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen;
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and became a fistula, and there was an emission and wind.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I used the information I had to treat him, and did not stop applying the poultice until he was well, and bound up the wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient had done him harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no illness, but he recovered in good health, and eating and drinking well;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and said no experimenters that when he has a small wound in the intestines, it must be tied in some way:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	Take the skin from a large testicle, and then gather the lips of the wound together,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the skin has opened the mouth, so it is placed on the .iij. lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches her mouth out;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he cuts off the head, and this stays there so it cannot come loose,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then you put another one in that same way as before, until the wound is completely healed;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound;
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This passage seems to be describing a surgical technique for treating intestinal wounds without causing any harm to the patient. The text is in Old French and dates back to the 12th-13th centuries.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and can tie the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this thread of intestine that is not yet shredded,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie at the head of this thread. i. a very fine linen thread, twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then dip the thread in the needle, and cut the intestine, and pull it through the slit.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of suturing frets is valid only as long as the vein and the hope remain;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no more cure than surgery.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	for fistula or wherever it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	That all wounds or abscesses, when they heal, are called universally "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most often when it is cut and the blood runs.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the theory of vital force, hard and white, so that one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also chewed like the feathers of an owl;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and not once in a clear sky, and another time in thick fog;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	ne either time, and another time enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is only by one of these seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	This is the translation of the provided Old French text:
ou por sa malice;	or, because of its malice.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or, because it has hard teeth and lips, so that it does not let them grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or, where there is too much bowels.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	If the legs are swollen, and the material is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	the medicine is not good for the cure;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because corruption is a way to cause disease;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because property in the region is late in digestion, and late in health, and by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already described all these causes, and the signs, and remedies of medicines in the dissection.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I should inform you of the cure for fistula, which is made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all limbs of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	For there are fistulae which come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the belly, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the back bone, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it is necessary to cut at the root of the member and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas which are of this kind are of great difficulty in healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is no fistula that does not come up to the level that I have said, and you have begun to heal it,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it clearly, take a piece of leather or iron, if the fistula is straight, try it out.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, try it out with a thin piece of leather.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	For the plons are wetted by the rain in the tortuosity.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if they pricked with a sharp needle and you cannot see it well by the tent,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if the cautery is applied to one of the punctures,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For if the moisture comes from one puncture to another, and cleanses it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	and then you will have bleeding under control, that you know if there are any bones or nerves, and it is shaved completely,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you squeeze his hand, and the place where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know for sure the place, whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein;
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in some cases that I have told you, if the cup is according to what I said,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and there are bones broken and rusted wheels that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the cure until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and its fistula is very deep from the right side, so that you cut it perfectly, as well as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then dip them wet in medicinal vinegar, and pour them up to the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the excess that is held up at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put oil-of-olives on holy chalk, as long as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not made well with this, then burn with fire, as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the nose is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein is injured or a limb is broken, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and darkness, let the king wait until the corruption is completely bone;
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal of things that trouble him as long as he is well;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not well, and reset it in the same way as before;
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	since you have not yet gone down to the well,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all corruption, then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that corruption is complete, so you cannot come.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other device than to weaken by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone that has rotted, and you can pull it with tweezers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is done with an appropriate instrument for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if he has one arm, if he can't walk, don't leave any of them.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	if moisture makes him clumsy, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if he has pain and moisture and heat, and delivers the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you don't remove them in an hour, put something that causes putrefaction on the wound,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it so long that the legs are inside the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will come together more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you only reset the corruption as long as the blackness is all bone,
puis restoure la plaie;	and then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is much decay of the bone, and it comes up to the root of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it covers all the way to the root of the bone, and then heals it until it is solid;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg;
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may obtain an example and aid for your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	A young man of about thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg from an cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	As the matter came to the leg, and was driven out by a large abscess, and had no apparent cause for opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	However, because of his madness, he opened so much that the abscess opened;
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and when they corrode the matter, and become a fistula, and I came out of the breach that all go up bow and moisture from the chest;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and much mirth did I find cure in.1 . years, and there was no profit for me in the art of surgery,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	for as long as I have been called, and saw his leg, and the medicines with which he was cured,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which corrots through the breaches into the chest;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body became red with youthfulness, and had a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I lit a tent in one of those passages, and then searched all the passages,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came out against the other on both sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and entered into one of the passages as far as I could see a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it rotten and putrid, and the putridness went as far as the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew who showed me the rotten bone, and I made sure that there was no other corruption, except for the one that I had;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with sodden medicines over a long period of time, and I could not seal it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the continuous corruption in the bone, and the sawdust, and then I sawed the bone, and leaned to weld the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not stop the blood flowing from a palm of the bone, and I carried it all the way down.

dou feu	double fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head should be positioned either forward or backward,
