puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then chop the bone with a suitable saw for this, and then heal as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The two ways in which it comes together by nature, by joining of wound, or by fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you chop this joint together, if it is joined according to its natural form;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or drapes dipped in oil so it doesn't stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two thin pieces of cloth until the joins are stuck together as is right.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The two pieces should be pressed together with the palm of one hand so that it sticks properly as is right.
Des vils	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large wrapped full of melancholy superfluities, which come from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more comes in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you give no spurious purging of the colon, and then heal the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The cure of iron is according to these two ways: one is to drink it mixed, and the other is to run black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you hold the vein, and tie it all up tightly.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size should be according to this method: raise the first leg of the patient very strong with hot water, until the large vein is clearly visible.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then strain the leg of the patient from above the knee down to the ankle;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then cut the vein in one place, or in two places, or in three places, of a width that is wide;
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	and then take out with force the black blood from your hand, from one side to the other, as much as the virtue of the disease allows you to suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then burn it, and command that he turns his meat black with coal;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and then restart the evacuation and sweating when the veins are clean, and give the medicine to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The method of applying the remedy is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then put it in a bath, and raise his leg with hot water until it turns red, and swollen veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you don't have a bath, heat it on the fire, and then put it on the affected area from the ankle to the knee, or in the part below the ankle at the foot;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then soak the skin with vinegar, and scrape the vein from each side until it feels smooth when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and if it turns red and black, and when it enters or leaves the skin it seems as white as a rope;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	and bottle up the roast as long as it is lean meat, and then dip it in a light wine,
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cover with another 1/4 of an ounce; then peel the skin from the vein as long as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then dip in roast at an angle as you did, and dip in another ounce, as you did first time;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cover with another size, or more if you need it, then peel the meat, and cover with two ounces of wine on the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	and then cut the tail and leave it at the second size; then take it out size by size until it is all finished, then cover it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then tie a strong double thread of thread to it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and leave it and cut it, and twist it with the thumb, and turn your hand from side to side, until it is all finished;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep it from unraveling, for if it unravels, then you cannot draw it out or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have finished treating it, put a wet wool cloth, soaked in wine and oil, on the wound's place; and let the cure go on until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vision is twisted and contorted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	if you split it badly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have described before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron that you cover the vision with if it is curved, and do not cut it, so that it covers the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large circumference, because if it were thin, it would split the vein, but being thick as we said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in legs, warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it grows in other parts besides the legs, and this causes a peeling that comes from the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If he comes from within the body snake-like and downward, protect between skin and leather.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of this injury are that it comes in the leg a very great swelling,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then change their faces, and begins the injury to come out, also like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head opens, if you wrap a piece of linen around one third and a half up to two thirds, and tie it on,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the ball hanging at the leg, and every time that it is there to the side, if the wrapper wraps around the ball and the new;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too far away, so that a part of it, and wrap the rest, and do not cover it all the way up to its root, as long as it is all out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cover it, so that it enters into the charnel, and brings about abscession and rot where it is, and bad sickness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because for this thing it is necessary that she be treated little by little up to the head, and there remains nothing or bones;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and this vein is never done when it comes to .v. palms long, or .x.,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and here are some fine people who have come to me, of whom she is of .x. long palms, and when you chop them, if they are short or large, and pierce until it is deep,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything is removed; and let the matter which is within be empty, and introduce into it remedies for any kind of corruption each day, then heal it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And never do this vein with hands wet, and certainly not when she opens at the joint of the foot, or where the foot is.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and the wind comes from the east, and from which it rains; treat it then as we have said above.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and cloth
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "buffalo disease", because it often affects buffaloes,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and cloth, and it goes everywhere, ascending and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and the pain is very great from one limb to another, until it tears the skin where it goes, and makes a loud sound.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is infected with pus, as if it comes from within, winding itself in and out, and sending forth worms and scabies or parasites.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and there is doubt of its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the neck:
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	and in due course enters and destroys the throat; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you cure and extract it, if it can only be done when he is:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So that you can put the joint in place again with a strong rope, tightly wound,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	and then turn it over and over, and if it does not fit perfectly into the frame,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so that the fire cautery on it as long as it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm he causes, if he ruins oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see him coming with his head near the oil, then remove his eye completely, then cut it off and throw it away;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and use the patient of purification of water of medicine solutions for bad humors to come out;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if meat is rotten.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vacir" in our land, and it is a pain that affects certain members.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and it spreads from one member to another; and I saw the one I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and .i. shortly thereafter, the eye rises up like a snake to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	as soon as possible, also as if it were alive silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that place and enters into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it runs through all the body, until it came out in the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	And he told me that it twists around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how much it moved from limb to limb, for I have never seen this disease move like that before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I know of many who have had pain in one place and then in another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I have never seen it happen like that, as I saw it happen to the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was for this reason that the woman had a dry breast, and the veins uncovered.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason does she seem to be constipated?
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear to be constipated according to this reasoning, but these who are delicious, and have dry breasts and veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you treat this disease, and the patient feels pain as we have described,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the lion lies down and does not get up again, and then it copes with him as long as that wind forces him to lie down.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the lion; and if you do not see his eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	For the cure of this person who causes wind, as if they were pills of putrid meat, and pills of seraphim, and similar things.
Des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of them is such that there are some with large points, and others small, and some curved, and some soldered.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some with .ij. angles, and some with tongues, and some where there are pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and some that strike in any member so strike according to .ij. ways: or in a principal member chews,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Here is the translation of the first sentence in your text:
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When there is a loss of sensation in any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, then you know:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you wash yourself with water from a spring, for death comes after many preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when there is no sign of death, and the arrow has not been completely extracted, if you tie it and clean the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and the medicine that is on the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when scotomy and pain and stiffness and redness in the joints, and inflammation and redness in the tongue, and spasm and confusion of thought, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes it comes from the nostrils or ears; and sometimes it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and sometimes there is a wet white spot on the wound, resembling pus, and sometimes it looks like burnt flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, if you hold it for a cure, and treat the arrow if it is not in place.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or curls is that it is near the left breast and also feels like it is wedged into something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and if the arrow changes as well as a bird, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and faints:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	says ahead of time that death might come.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow is that it does not feel pain in the palm, but when it jumps out of the wound there is foam, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he breathes heavily and shudders with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters into the shoulder blade's cover, it severs the little ribs; and causes great pain and sorrow and heavy breathing; and all the limbs shake.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters into the stomach, perhaps there is foam jumping out of the wound, indicating that it has gone astray and not struck the target.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters into the abdomen, and in jumping out of the wound there is no end to the intestines, then there is no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters the bladder, and the urine flows out in spurts and he runs away, and the patient feels great pain, you know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, as it is the case with the face and neck and throat and shoulder and ajutoire and spine and forelegs and legs, and similar body parts, are safe according to several arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow enters the neck or artery, and it is not fatal, as I will tell you what happened to me, so that you do something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	He had an arrow choked or cut in the root of the neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and the other side sewed up the fat of the ear, and he was healed without feeling any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I sewed up a piece of meat that had gotten into the fat of the oil, separating the paper from it.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was withdrawn, and I could only get to the tip towards the wood.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was blue-green in color, very light in weight without ears; the game was healed, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And cut an arrow from the throat of a Christian man, and the arrow was Arabic to the ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I knew the armpits, and I tested it until I cut it, and the Christian man was cured.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And cut an arrow at the hip, which went through his belly or chest, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then he lived for three hundred years, but his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrow, and set it in place, and drew it back, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to see a man who has an arrow shot through his buttocks or anus, and the wound is well healed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and let the arrow remain inside, and do not change its natural state;
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	do not find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I see another man, to whom he shot an arrow into his face, and it was sewed up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and it remained thus without suffering much pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And shot an arrow at a prince's son, the king, which went through his neck, but missed his heart.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly倾斜着向右边；而且箭头完全扎进去了。
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat after she had been ill for two days. The wound was very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I asked her to open her mouth wide, and I did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt pain and discomfort on the right side of her ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of an arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the plaster of troy to the chest for this reason so that the lungs do not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I discovered the lungs from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster every day, and quickly resolve the wound, and delay it for a long time for the patient,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he feels the arrow; and I tell him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a caustic medicine by hands, as long as it was open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried, and felt the head of the arrow which moved to its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I put on the wound by that caustic medicine, as long as the head of the arrow was clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and I traversed well the terms for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then unwrapped it with a wound I had tied up with thorns, and the flesh on either side, and it couldn't be pulled out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I stopped using sharp tools and devising methods to remove it until I got a good pair of pliers.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its shape will be after the end of this chapter, as long as I kept it in my hand and returned the wound to its place.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the judge said that the cartilage at the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I healed it then, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Tell me about the quality of extracting certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you apply my remedy to those I do not mention here, for the book cannot include everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	But the master sages compare only a few things, and those that are present and failing;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	trueve nueve oevre, et nuef instrument, au dessendement des choses extrangies qui avienent en cet art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the arrows should not come from the members where they are inserted except according to the following four ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or by another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes in by one way, when it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and does not go in again at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, if it leaves it as the fur is rotten inside, and let the issue come out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, if you leave it like this for some days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, if there is a small hole inside everywhere, as long as the inside space is widened, and then the treatment is applied;
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes through one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said to avoid in the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it as long as it is even for a few days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes only to the flesh, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	and if the arrow does not go deeper than the bone, and only comes to the flesh, that is death.
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient will last for some days without any other bad accident, if the mechanism of drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck so that it cannot come out, then administer tar and resin, as I have told you; then heal the joint as long as it remains healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is re-embedded in the body so that it cannot be seen, and you seek it throughout the whole body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you can feel it, and with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by the pressure of the wound, and for the sake of the arrow's depth;
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein, if the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and train the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the shaft is lodged in the muscle at a depth of .ij. parts from the tip that you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully though you do not break the arrow, that you draw it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot take it out at once, so that the end of the arrow is stuck in his flesh, then draw it out, for extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of extraction makes you uncomfortable, then apply what we have said about the cure in our chapter on the paste;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against incising the nerve and the vein, and do not attempt to draw out the arrow without risk;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If it is hot or cold, or firmly or painfully; and put the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow went in,
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	For an arrow that comes from another part, or does not open anything of it, or the skin is swollen in a particular place, if we see it or feel it:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore cut along, as long as the scrapes can take it, and then remove it: but now jump back.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be removed, let it rest, and then begin the extraction again as long as it can be;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a arrow in it, blow it out completely;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if there is a knot, and you know how to cut it, so you administer the instrument well;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	So that the arrowhead goes into the hole of the instrument; and then pour out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is cut, so that the instrument with a point entering it, for to rejoice the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, so that you cut all the charm around where the venom is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it covers, if it is possible.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow pierces where the pelvis or bladder or ribcage is, and it is close by, then you can cover over it, if you cover.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and don't cover the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, that is a job.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to remove arrows is similar to an eye, and this is how you should do it:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the pointed hair is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For binding the point of an arrow, so that it resembles the feather of a bird, thus is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for bending and for holding, so that it can be shaped like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common heart
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one heals are xxxiii, so that there is a head xvi.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is to know: i.i. bones that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbeche".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the ii.i. arteries that are in ii.i. temples apparent;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and .ij. veins that are in .ij. nails of .ij. hairs, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the head;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the 2. veins that are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the 2. veins that are on top of the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and there are veins that are torn.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly known as  are found in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it runs along the left side of the body, and it is called by the common people "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the other is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it "vein of comfort"; and if the base is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it "vein of the navel", and it is over the heart.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and that is which is opened in front of the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the small vein is the one that is between the thumb and the index finger, and if it has three rains.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot are .iij. veins: one is desoz the corbeure doupochet de senestre costit
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one, which is at the ankle of the right coast; and the vein that is called «nesse», which is in the ankle of the other coast;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are .iij. veins desoz those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	and the vein that is called  «sainie», which is behind the ears, and it has a headache and migrain.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the patient, as I told you, and it is that you reset the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are with a sharp cloth; then tie up the patient's neck with a strap,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the .iij. veins appear behind the ears in .iij. places depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then feel for the pulse on both sides, and where you feel the pulse pulsating on one side, sign;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	and take the lance, and pierce through the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand all along the vein upstream,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut off and tie up the flesh and the vein well .ij. two must travel, and let out blood as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then extract and bind it together, as long as it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood vessels that are in the two temples, if they cause migraine headaches,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and eye pain, and a sore throat, and water coming from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the vessel if it is like this:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	is that the patient's neck is stretched out so that the two veins open up widely.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and send the hair above the nose to grow long, and then sign with the hand.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then place the curette on the vein at the top of your index finger, and dip the lance into water,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and place the vein at the top, and cut it, like you did in .ij. other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then remove the curette, and place your index finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then let it form, and leave it until it is healthy; and we have spoken of them and their cutting and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the front vein is as good as the health of the cerebral veins from the ancient diseases of the face, and has headaches and dizziness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and hold firmly with your hand, or some other object, and let the blood flow in the amount that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut off the neck of the patient, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame must not be too hot; and the vein is cut across, because the bone is close by, and the flame might break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The five veins that are in the five limbs should be tied together, and at the base of the neck, and to the taste, and to the redness, and to the oil, and to the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is that the patient pulls his neck out by twisting it from any rope, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	and then the health, and be the health of the traveler, a little of the long flame a little wide, because there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, in case of a breeze; then make the blood run, as much as you need, and then tie it to the cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The health of the vein of the new born baby should be measured, and if it is too big or too small, and if there are any diseases on the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	if as headache and brightness that comes to the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the disease is that the patient twists his neck, then hold his nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long thin flame, and burn between the iij. nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein does not open well on its own, and now the blood will begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not overheat it too much, and make it run a bit of blood according to your need, then leave it a night, for it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	is the form of the fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The five givens in the form of fire: aid in the stranglehold of the larynx, and in the obstruction of speech, and many diseases, and impetigo, and ulcers, and herpes, and are to be used.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the fire so that the disease is removed from the neck on both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master stand over the patient's head, and the patient cuts with .i. a scythe,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then he heals the vein of the long one widely then soon of blood, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then he repairs the other in the same way, then he draws out the ligaments carefully, and holds them so that they do not move;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	let the patient rest; and in the morning the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On the health of deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	On the health of lips: to prevent chaps from forming on the corners of the mouth, and from corroding the gums, and from splits in the lips, and from nosebleeds and headaches.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of this remedy are to make the patient sit in front of you, and to hold his throat as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two openings, which are on the right and left lips.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and the eyes look like they are black, and because of the small veins around them that are black:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	so cope both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so cope the largest of each pair, and do the same for the .ij. veins that are above and below, because it is a similar method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the small ones on top
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	For the blood vessels that are opened with the tongue after opening the cerebral vein, and this is in the extraction of the throat, and in the diseases of the eye, and in the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the surgeon is that the patient dies between your hands before the sun, and the tongue turns blue, and looks down at each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So then both sides, and do not over-surge, for the veins are there.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck which are commonly operated on are operated on according to .ij. manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the width and the stretching of veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is like this, and it is wide as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And has the skill to open the flat veins that are visible with great blood flow, and that contain large blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and it is for saving subtle veins, or there is subtle blood yellow.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The salve of the basilica, which is one of these veins, soothes diseases that are found in the throat, neck, chest, and stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the healer to heal thoroughly, and to warm himself with the artery that is found.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts into the artery, and blood flow comes, if it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be held by fire but cut off as much as possible.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the base does not open clearly, if it is necessary to remove it and change it with another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you do not want any rain of his, or you heal in the place of his the vein by cutting off the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the coat to the flame ansile, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	and if you know the place of the injury, so that you extract the arm, that you touch the place as soon as you know the hair;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the head, and then draw the arm, and coat the vein with the flame ansile;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and guard against injuring in the artery when you see the head dislocated, for it is from the artery: beware of it. So as not to.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see coming out on top as urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	So hurry up, and place your hand on top for a long time, then remove your hand so that it does not hurt, because this often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	So raise the limb up and leave it there, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move him until he is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the limb is not stable, and it comes to you, and the medicine is not given to you, then open the artery, for the head of the shoulder is dislocated; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a strip of fig bark, cut it, and take one half and tie it firmly together up to the other day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If there is no bleeding, it is good; if not, use the powder that stops bleeding; as we have said,
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the bleeding does not become greater in many situations because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The treatment for a vein in the middle is to place the finger with the wound at the base of the neck, and around the heart.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	for it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it comes to the surgeon that he should cut down on the nerve which is exposed, and if he cuts too much in perfection, and then it bleeds;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the patient becomes gray, and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and the nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man by its subtlety, then you must cut it with an anesthetic; and avoid cutting the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two thirds, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment of a headache with the help of fire, that it pulls away from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is appropriate to hit with fire from the olive or from the merlin flame, because it is the most effective for all veins, since it does not damage the nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest fire first, and do no harm the first time, and start over again;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and in case it increases the length of some men's penises for the first time but does not harm them.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your belief.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about a doctor is that medicine should only be practiced to maintain health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent diseases from arising;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the surgeon make it in one of the three veins that are in the head: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basal.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the surgeon must make it at the beginning of fasting, and in autumn and winter after supper when the sign of fullness appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and the surgeon must make it on the first day or the third day, after two hours or three days a day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The surgeon who is amined for certain diseases has no fixed term, but it must be done at the beginning of the day or night in all hours and times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one should not save children until they are 12 years old, nor a woman unless she has been pregnant for four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not save the elderly who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And if one is to be saved in any way, it is necessary that the intestines of a light clister be destroyed.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if it has suffered from a foul wind, so that the veins do not draw the superfluous dung that is harmful to the main members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k'il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k'il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	car il y a plusors mores qui sont souvens, comme la colique et le vomissement, et le decorrement de ventre, et la multiplicatie d’abiter a femme, et le traval, et veiller et juner;
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and to keep the flesh of the foot dry from the wound at the third toe, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and to protect yourself from work, hunger, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be lying down and jointed, and may the surgeon be above you, and rub your arms. 12 times or 13,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then remove the ligature gently, for when it is too tight or constricted, it cannot run without being removed.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with hands, until the veins swell, and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then soak the wound with a little old oil, then put your index of your left hand on that wound to rub it where you want to heal,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	to make sure that the vein is not cut and does not bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like strings to the skin, and if any such are damaged, they will bleed profusely.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if one puts out the flame, then removes it, and cannot open the vein, then is he among those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if one opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, so that he may be warned of the need for care in such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, if it begins again a little later on that same side or during treatment, if the legs are swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the legs are swollen, and the patient hopes to recover, let him lie for a day or two, and do not bind his arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	For adventure I will come out of the chest; no bath, then start the cure if it pleases her.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the break is small, or the blood runs subtlely and you doubt that it will not run as much as you see, so confident in this very break, right up to the full flame;

Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the leg swollen, do not restart the cure, and put a little oil thereon, for it softens the body of the blood, and is fresh in this leg where the oil is placed, because she smoothes the course of the blood, and is moistened by this oil.

Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid putting on anything of what we have said, because perhaps in the court without the artery; but make it.I. dry by applying plaster to harden the place, then heal it with other remedies until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And each of the three must be used according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it run until it is red; and if you see a lump, let it run until it is thin; and if it is too thick, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are pale and have a need to extract blood, one should make the wound larger and wider, and make the flames wide.

et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of treatment saves from decay of the flesh and destruction of the nerves, and it is better than long or wide surgery.

et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and employ other things that we have spoken of in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If it vomits up arms, and sometimes also, if it is weak enough, that it heals little by little, according to the quantity of its continuing virtue.

Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if it heals on another part, it must heal three times a day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and it brings on a fever. If this quantity is drawn in great amount, and the opening enlarged until it comes out in small drops;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	And that you keep all of the conditions of health, and put your hand on his pulse as it heals, so that death does not come out in small drops;

ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is hoarse, let him stretch his arms weitly, for it would be ill.

et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .i. piece of silk wet with water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has been pricked, do not hold it, but let it rest until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing blood a second time, then the vein in the middle, or another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The arm is veined where it connects to the shoulder; therefore, draw blood from there if it is composed of veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way to prepare the vein is that the patient dips his hand in warm water until the pulse becomes faint;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then stretch the skin gently so that the vein appears clearly; then cut it now, not wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the split be wide, and let the wound be well near the joint of the hand, and so it cannot come out, put the hand in warm water, and let the blood run into the water as long as you have enough of it;

et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the wound from this vein is safer from all other wounds, that there is no artery or nerve;
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	the saving of the right hand wound from all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Here is the translation of the first line of the text:
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you cross-slice it all, do not hurt anything."
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not cut too deeply, lest the nerve be damaged, for they are all naked under the skin."
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand back in hot water, which freezes it into the wound, and cannot be taken out."

Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood of him in the left hand belongs to the disease of the mouse, and do all the same as I told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the woman belongs to all the diseases that are caused by the horse,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the mare, and retention of flowers, and disease of the rain, and of the cocks and old legs, and similar diseases.

et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on top of the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and up to the foot in many places;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So that it goes deeper or wider, or at the ankle, so that it must be cut more deeply.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it on the foot, so that the wound is deep and wide, and cut it as one would in a field; and let the flames burn.

ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerve, if it bleeds too much, as we have said, and so do the same thing with the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood of the vein is at the ankle, and its sap is worth the pain of the thigh, when it comes to pain.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of his leg is that the patient goes or bathes, and removes from above the ankle .iiij. two in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise does not open the vein; and if it opens, so that you can heal it in all ways that you can, and by crossing;

Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not heal it, so that the leech is above or below the foot, and toward the small ear, and guard against the water;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much blood that you see, and then untie the link, and put on cotton and hold it in place; now he is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuums of suction
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or glass, or marble; and the suction is applied according to 3.1 ways: either by hurting and pulling out blood, or without hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this type of suction that is without hurting is according to 3.1 ways: either it is all fire, or it is not fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation which is made by piercing and by extraction of blood so is made in 123. days from the heart,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	for one is all in some the head; and others is half the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and 1 other on 1 coast of the neck; and the windpipe separates the mouth;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the windpipe separates the shoulders; and the windpipe under the chin;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the suction cups extract the .ij. arms; and the suction cups of the .ij. legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the suction cups of the .ij. ankles; and the suction does not treat blood, except that of small veins that are scattered over the cart,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason do not feel faint, as one feels when opening a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it does not need to be eaten, nor does it need to be drunk, in any disease that comes from overindulgence, until the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if because of necessity due to disease or by custom, we administer it every hour during the month, or at its end and in between;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to vomit, become very ill;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who have vomiting and redness on their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and if there are those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue has fled, and they are parched with thirst;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who think and see blood and vomit and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is half past noon, we order them to exhale after.iij. hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The physician of the mother should not help in the birth of the child ... that comes to the hairs, and it is not until after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation is in place for the physician of the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not good for those who are of cold complexions to use it or who have had a fever, because this does them much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and so it is not good for those who are old to use it, or who have had any cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured of it often become confused, and therefore the cautery should be placed a little further back due to the confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The placement of the cautery at the base of the neck is good for diseases of the throat and tonsils, and also for treatment of the mouth.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and from the splitting of the channel of the pommel, and all the rest, and repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to put it in with force, for if it holds too firmly, then there will be difficulty or obstruction or stomach or elsewhere.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventsations are like .ij. ribs of the neck if it hurts as much as the pain in the head, and blinding and throbbing, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the place of the health of the church; and it is necessary that you command to the saint that he express his hand to put on, so that he does not cut the artery, and does not bring damage from blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The windings of the mouth are very much affected by disease of the mouth, and the corruption of the gums, and other diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place where the lower lip meets the upper.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are affected by disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The windings of the sides affect as much as the three veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command to the surgeon that he does not cut too much perfectly, for his veins are naked of flesh and know how to stop bleeding.
