Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	and the suction cup that is on the back so vale as emoroydes from the foundation, and of disease suet, and it should be a great one, and be of leather, that has a good business of well sucking; and by chance, if it were subtle, then would it break; and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs so open, for they draw blood from all the body, and are worth for ancient pains of the hips, and of the knee, and of the bladder, and remove the flowers; and they are in the place of the two feet, and moreover they weaken the body after a long time, and bring about death in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of putting the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and suck quickly, and place it firmly, and stir evenly, and do not cease to do so, until you see the red and inflamed spot, and appear the pain of blood; then stop, and remove the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some who have a dark color, and clear pores: so it is necessary to cut once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if he is out of breath, then he should strike 19 times: the first time to make a path for heavy blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if he is very heavy, then he should strike the third time; and when we want to squeeze out blood little by little, we should only press once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want to squeeze out blood, we should do so frequently; and if he is heavy, we should strike firmly, and the blow should be such that the heart is pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover those with thick and tough skin, who have been pricked by needles, that you rub the joints with oil that softens and dissolves.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	Here is the translation of the first sentence of the text in Old French into English:
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	if it is in the liver, of oil of sorrel, or of larkspur, or of chamomile, or other similar matter.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	and if the surplus is thick and cold, then take oil of amber, or of balsam, or of aniseed, and similar matters.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	and if the meat is tender and large porridge, then it is not necessary to put oil in it:
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is necessary to wash after the windification of pink water, or cold water, or sloe water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other resembling.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture, if it is lifted thus, or with pink water, and with water of myrtle, and with sumac, and with resembling things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And he who has great excesses, are lifted by old wine, or with water of hawthorn, or with a decotion of fennel or chamomile, or other resembling things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to take a bath before the windification, but after the bath an hour or so; and do not sleep after windification.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and he must not go to bed, when he should be winded, nor when he is winded.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are ill-tempered, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he drinks cold things, as pomegranates, endive, and lettuce at the mint, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and warm wine, and ale of wheat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, if they drink syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and they juice little, and juice little and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will be wind-blown, if he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some people three times or more of an aromatic or musk before or after the wind, in order to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let it be subtle, but it is necessary that only those who are warm drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are not meant to hurt are those placed on the liver, and on the kidney, and on the podagra, and on the belly, and on the boudin, and on the reins, and on the hainche, for this member does not suffer pain from being cupped.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does it not more than to attract blood from member to member,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	if we put on the mammary glands when the child is stillborn; to remove the viscous substance that is in the member, if we put suction cups on the belly and on the boudin to reduce the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it relieves pain, when there is an operation or death, if by its attractive virtue the operation is relieved, or it moves away the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so he will do if he puts it on the liver and on the heart when there is wind trapped,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are emptied clean so that only a little; and never are they emptied together fire, and never are they emptied with sweet water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as the disease of pleurisy, and in such a way that he fills the suction cup with hot water or with water in which he has cooked herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And there are 21/4 inches of leather from the edge around the middle. A small hole as for an awl
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be of skin, smooth before it so that it does not cut the patient when put on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle is a staff of skin or iron to hold a candlestick,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the children's suction cups are different from the old ones, and leaner than the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must put this suction cup onto the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle of wax or .i. smoothly, and put it on the suction cup at the root of the penis which is on the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so it doesn't burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and your two hands are on the joint that we have said, so that when you see him, if there is steam, and take off the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the dressing off as before, and put it back on often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the case of the suction cup which is amine for pleurisy, there is no verge or hole, and it is only used when it is flat with water, and put on the limb as little as possible;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sansues are not applied except to limbs where it is impossible to use suction cups due to their smallness, as with lips and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the naked legs of a horse, as with two or three year olds, and others similar;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of using them so that when you find Sansues that are in clear fresh water, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into a bowl of clear fresh water, as long as they are familiar with it, and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then wash with water and vinegar, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clear, and are healing, then if it is possible to put a suction cup, then put it on, because that helps after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the limb, and then dip it in water, very well, and then squeeze it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is too warm after washing the skin, then wrap it in a cold linen cloth, and put on, until the skin is dry;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if it has a multiplicity of holes, then put on it crushed vitriol, or gall, and similar things until it is stopped.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half of peeled peas on the place, and leave them as they cook in the place, then now it will be stopped;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work to do, then take other waters.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the waters do not want to take it, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you put an needle in it as long as the water comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, if they burn.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	When you see that they are crying, sprinkle a little powder of allium and marjoram, or ash, so they will not cry now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	You must know, my son, that the wise men of old did not write of this medicine, nor have I ever read of it in any book.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the knowledge of this medicine is strange to us in our country, for I never found any good knowledge of it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing about it except from the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied and treated the science, and by experience, and by the customs of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and summarized it at the end, and clearly illustrated the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the preceding twenty chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is fitting that we say in this book the sum of the words and the chapters where wisdom is placed, and it remains on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture, dislocation, twist or sprain comes to someone, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from one side and the other, if nothing else stops him, so as not to be weak of heart, or feeble, or old;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if it is too tight or too loose; and if it is a cold weather, a cart drawn by oxen and covered with hides, and do not drink wine, nor eat any greasy foods, and do not fill yourself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the aphorism, nor about the expansion of matter in the member; if the disease returns to its first rule, which it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the sick person be nourished with foods that promote fatness, or they have viscosity, such as cooked flour in water, and rice, and beans, and peas, and poultry, and fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For if a person is too cold, it is better to prevent injury and do so more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken from age and decay cannot be well healed or strengthened according to their nature by the loss of members, nor those which are too tender, as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, repair the broken bone. I. large tendons which join and support the limb together, as much as possible so that it heals properly; and for this purpose there should be a lot of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that broken bones are of many kinds and in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is other than the break of the foot or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the hip, and another when it is sharpened, as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that is all a little cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And to each kind there is its own tool, and its own instrument for restoration, according as the memory comes back to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is caused by the breaking of the bone because the joints are twisted and open well from the sides, and press on with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or bumping, and the patient feels no great pain, it is not due to any fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well be due to twist, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not due to any twisting with the hand, but rather put medicines on it that come later, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that is in the shoulder, and these 3 parts are separated, now it is necessary to put them together evenly, so that the abscesses come out easily.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscesses have come out, then he should not rest for a day, until the abscesses are healed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then he should make it even with the knife that you can cut and trim lightly and carefully, and know that the healing of this is lighter than the healing of that which has pieces; then he binds it, as it is fitting hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	and if there is a bone with pieces broken, and if it is the hand or foot or any small member of the body, or two strings, or a string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are in place, by all means return them to their places with your tools, and be careful that by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the .ij. bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right: if it is stretched well and does not move too much, do not press it so much as those who work on it with fire and contraction of the member do, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, so strictly keep the patient that he does not move it, neither awake nor sleep, nor turn, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limbs are so secure that they feel no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when one feels no pain at all, almost not at all, and it is necessary to put in place the arrangement that one feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard well that it is put correctly, so that there is no twisting when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that there are various kinds of broken limbs, small and large and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs, and similar ones: it is necessary to wrap them in soft linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and for those who are fat, such as the chest and legs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and sturdy linen cloth, because the large linen envelops the entire limb, holding it firmly together so that there is no gap;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	and then tie them lightly in three or four turns around the limb, and hold one hand over all the linen, then go up to the break and tighten it less, so that the break is slightly pulled away from the hand; car il est bon que li membre ne soit pas trop estraint sous peine qu’il en soit dommageable;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the joint little by little, until you press hard on the sound part of the joint, then take another joint, and turn it back quickly on the broken one;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the sound part of the fracture and hold it gently, not too tightly or too loosely, as we said in the first joint above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then place between the joints of linen or drapelets, until they are all even, then tie it all together with a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something that soothes the swelling and leaves it alone for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then tie them to your poles, and be of half a long line made red, or of a mast that is used for sailing, or of palms, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the pole that one puts on the break is a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be also far away as necessary for the limb of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tie them to the poles also as you did with the first pole, then bind above a thread equally, as in the first pole on the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the thread gets tighter, then looser again; and it is necessary that the string be neither too thin nor too thick, and that it be soft.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the string is thick, as I have seen in works of fools who make their cords out of twisted linen threads, and that is a great mistake, because the thread cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it only comes to between each stone less than two inches of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the nails in his bones after the extraction in his health, so do not put them together with linen, or woolen cloth, so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the wound is broken, I will tell the cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to extract all the members of the body on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not good to put on braces before 5 or 10 days, or more according to the severity of the abscess, and in a few days it will have healed.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and this is the method of the ancient braces for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour which holds to the walls of the mill, and confound it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and that is the common method of the brace restoring the fracture to many conditions, and most of all to women and small children, for it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of the brace restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take Z barars and lanolin and knotgrass and asfetida and gum arabic and myrrh, Z.Z.Z.; mirr and aloe, Z.v.Z.; alychil Z.viiij.Z.; and make a powder of them, and mix it with plenty of egg; this composition of the meat is hot, so use this brace, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones gently, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plasters that is worth: take mugwort and chamomile, 1/10th Z. mirrra and aloe, 1/7th Z.; acacia vi. Z., well ground, and confit with oil or lots of honey, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of plasters that is effective for dislocated joints and broken bones: take a young lamb, and moil it in water and oil, and put it on the joint. These plasters do not help, but they are good to soothe hot abscesses and properly treat pain in the bone.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making plasters to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way of making plasters to heal broken bones and reduce inflammation: take roots of chamomile, violettes, times, and wheat; grind them together with a little wine, and apply it to the member that is warm. Alternatively, grind the roots with oil, and apply it to the joint with a little honey or oil of coriander.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way to make plasters more strongly than the first, when the wound of the member comes to restoration. Take roots of plantain, and seeds of flax, buckthorn, melilote, and sycamore-bark, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and grind them up, and confect with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that one should not put plaster on a broken member more strongly than the wax and oil cerots, and nothing else, and he says that it must be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should put on a broken member things dry and warm, such as mirr, aloe, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plasters for an injury and pain: take mugathon and horses' hooves, or feathers of ospreys, and plantain seeds, and wheat, all in equal parts; grind them up, and make plasters with it, and lay it on.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then pull it a little way apart, and see that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the jaw moved out of its place; if not, pull it by the hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if the pain or itching comes to a head, or there is no relief or swelling, then make haste and pull it apart and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of sea water, and dip it into the water, and raise up the jaw, until the itching ceases, and the pain is eased;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then leave the member to rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with water or rose oil, and tie it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and rest the inflammation of the member, and be sure that the pain is gone, then start again with a gentle cautery, and a little plaster, and do not pull it out too strongly as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need to plaster and bind it, then start again, as you did at first, with even binding.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If it does not come to the member at all, or only after three days or four days, and never more than ten days; according to what you see, as long as the break-up is slow, and the shoulder approaches the socket from below;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then you must restrain it more than before, and make its meat grow thicker, as I have said above; and if you see that the leather dries up more quickly than is necessary, know that the joint is coming together again;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then let it rise in warm water every time you release it, and let it rest for three days, and put salt on it;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	For this work, therefore, let the member be cut off at its root, and carefully what it has twisted, so that it returns the member to its place: this is bad, and if it is done with fear, and I see no other thing than to allow it to heal and to treat it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways to break something, and there are different shapes and causes, and they are distinguished.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by the impact of an axe, and the collarbone is broken all the way through until it reaches the shoulder blade, just as it happens with a hatchet; and for this reason it is called "hatchet break".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear breaks through bone from above and is called in this way "absolute"; and the wound is of these great or small two breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact inside, or a blow from above or from the root of a stone, or from sitting on a stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing break, which comes close to the tendon that is outside the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that enters the bone slightly, as fine as a hair, and this break is called "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is caused by a stone, or by falling, or by some other thing, and causes a piece of bone to come out, and the head of the bone becomes displaced as the blacksmith does when he works on the bellows; if it enters between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those whose bones are moist at the top, so that they become deformed as the head of a child does.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and in all these ways of breaking, small pieces are formed, just like tiles, and I will speak about their treatment in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaking by traction on them, and inquiry into their causes, and by the horse corrumpe who is above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is caused by what happens when the bone is uncovered and rubbed upon. If the fracture is blackened, it will appear so.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, beware of accidents that may occur in patients, and if you do not see any bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, palmsiness, feverishness, and hairs standing on end, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, they cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any promising accident, and if you expect healing to begin, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the break comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most so that you can heal.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the chest, you must hurry to open the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone does not rot, and the accident that we have spoken of comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the tissue that covers the skull, then it is necessary that you split the broken part so: and this is that you squeeze the head of the sick person, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more suavely than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if the discharge of blood comes up when the bone is uncovered, or an abscess forms, help him with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with wet cloth soaked in oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And make the wound rest as long as the abscess is calm, and are sure of the discharge of blood; then begin to cut the bone, and it is done according to 1.j. ways of work: one way is that you chop at the narrow end before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I pour .I. another amount, as great as the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different measurements, some are long and others are wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron; and in working lightly, so that you don't bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is sharp and hard, so that you pierce it from within, as well as you bring together measurements with filets, not perfectly so that they pass beyond the bone at the back of the head, and must have a margin or a circle on top, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each comes in its place at the back of the bone, so that you have filets for all test: and there are the 3 methods of filets:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce within the bone is that you put 1 filet on the bone, and turn back your two hands as much as you know that the bone has been pierced; then remove the filet a little further away, and so do all around, then cut off the space of the bone that is between the openings, and do this more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you take the bone in your hand, or any of the tools that you have, such as pliers, tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have the bone pierced and treated, if you know that you retain the sharpness that is delayed from the bone to all .i. other instrument resembling an incisive, but it is necessary that it be more soft and more subtle than the other incisive;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it does not delay anything from the small bones, nor any scales, if the bone is slightly damaged by one of the instruments; then heal the wound with a lot of oil and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of opening it is that which Galen mentions, which is more effective; and press it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where the break opened; so that when you have discovered that part, you put on the end of this lens-shaped incision, from which this form comes:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And don't cut from one side, and are the two sides of the flesh, so that the cutting is next to the bone; then, raise a small mallet above it, so that you gently strike the bone all around, and take great care of the tendon that is attached to the bone.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is injured to the bone, so that the bone is slightly broken, because the bone does not hurt easily, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone does not break through to the skin, and the bone is cut slightly from above, and there are small pieces, then smooth it with a sharp razor, of which you must have different quantities, to adjust each one according to the injury and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are more sharp razors, and then even smaller ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair tresses and subtle cuts, you must bring forth reason according to their treatment; and this is a thing that has not yet been answered to those who have placed their studies in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the medicine is uncovered, you must take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in oil and put it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another doubled cloth, or two, and wet it in wine and oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do so lightly that you do not injure the medicine, then apply a third one, and do not stretch it out except to the extent that it covers the wound alone;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it for one or two days until the pustules are calmed, then remove it, and apply medicines as roots of herbs, and flour of times, and powder of incense, and aristolog, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and apply medicines immediately without biting;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	and guard that the wound be well-cleansed, so you do not leave it oozing, nor do you let it assemble the bow, for when the bow assembles over the web of the skull, if it is corroded and worn, it brings great harm to the patient; for when one puts on a medicinal sharp thing, if it stops above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care, therefore, that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the blackness comes only because of the medicine that has been put on, which has virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and iii parts of rose oil and bind i drape of it to the medicine.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then let the medicine be cured in the way that suits it, until it is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Saiches that no time are broken the .ij. parts of the neck above, or the one by the sole, because they are .ij. bones; and that bone is cartilage, and does not break unless it is forced or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the 2.ij. parts is broken, it is necessary that you stop your small finger or hurt from the neck, and put it equally in between your index finger and thumb, and towards the outside, until the neck revives according to its natural form;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the broken part is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot come to its place, then it is necessary that you make it equal to the top of a small stick.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if his fracture is of one-half, if you do otherwise, and hasten to restore the first day if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or ninth day, when the abscess at the root has calmed down, then wrap it in linen cloths from the neck down, if his fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another with another from the other side, if his fracture is there; and let the cloths be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that there is no need to wet the cloths again, each day; it does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that the cloth be wet in sheep's fat and powder of millet; then leave the cloth, until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never put feathers in tents, and if you do, so be it. Take off the cover, and let the breeze blow on the patient; or make a knot as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess breaks out while you are working, so be it. Put cotton soaked in oil or a little bit of salve on it; or, as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if an abscess does not break out, put plaster on it from the outside, made of flour and powder of senna, mixed with alumen, then put it on light bandages, and do not tie the knot;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the knot is small and has broken into pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then cut the wound, and cure things that have been broken by it, and bind them together, and if necessary, put plaster on it and oil;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if he has not within him no wound whatever, if he is cured of fever, and I put hay for him, as long as he is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the rupture of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the fracture is not very great, and it is not broken into two pieces, but rather bent inwards, then you must gently set it back into place.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right side of the jaw, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand into the mouth, gently push the fracture inwards, and with the other hand push it gently to the right. Make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is a fracture of the mandible, it should be treated in .ii. parts, so that they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move, or there is a hole, then draw them out with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and put it on the broken jaw, and put 1. drapel double; and put on the drape a large well-made plate, or a piece of leather that is even, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind it at the muys you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the appearance has changed, then remove it on the third day, and then put back what has changed; and apply plaster, with powder from the mill, mixed with much egg white or flour of seed, after you have removed the cerote; and put on another light plaster, and if the plaster applies, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it for as long as it remains healthy; many times is healthy in 3 weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscesses burst, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, it is necessary that no piece of bone is broken; if subtle an ostable instrument is suitable for it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then open it with flame according to necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have broken all these bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, then put on it plasters suitable for him, to prevent infection, until he is healed.
de la forcele	forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	The broken joints are often forced forward, above the shoulder, and the breakage is according to 1.2 ways: or it is broken and dislocated in 1.2 ways, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound. And the overtaking is when the break is without a wound, that you have 1.2 ministers, so that one tints the shoulder joint that is broken forward; and the others extend the neck towards the part; then make the break even on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have the need to extend further, so put on the shoulder an oval piece of cloth, or linen, and let it be large according to your need; and they raise and hold firm the piece, and draw it towards your hand, so that you make even the break, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder to the far side, because it comes out completely, then it is necessary that the patient lie down on his side, and put the shoulder under a pillow, and place the ministers under the shoulder to hold it up; so that the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the break to your two sides, and if you find them broken, cut them with care; and carefully pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, use a tool like that of the incisor to put it back in place.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and make it like a spoon, and is not curly, and be also wide enough according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and have 1.5 inches, as you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, as is the split of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are confident about the incisions, if the wound is hot, and the split is small, or if you doubt about the incisions, if you cover the wound with linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot incisions come, if you soak .i. linen in oil and water and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very broad band of a palm's width, and then put thereon 2 drapails double-folded, and the enplaastre; then take a thin stake of 15 inches long, and wrap it around that band, so that the top of the band hangs down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put thereon the stake on the break, and turn the band on the neck, and desoz the asselle sainne, and desoz the asselle malaide; and the ramoinne of each one part, and when you see that the lieure holds the break in front, and you clearly see that the stake does not move upon the bone, then reward each day, and when the string slackens, if the restraint;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the malaide stand on his back, and let him put when he sleeps .i. small pillow desoz the asselle, to raise the ajutoire up; if the break is lightened by the aligement of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not loose it except in case of a bad accident, for .xx. days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	"Then begin the plastering of the shoulder if it has been displaced or is out of place, and only do so by touching it; shape the plaster according to the form of the displacement, and reset it according to its natural position in all ways that you can; then put on top of it powder from the mill with a lot of ash, and apply lightly, and put on a double cloth; then put on a wide and thin board, slightly wider than the shoulder, and release the board at the edge of the shoulder, so employ such a cloth as to cover the board evenly; and then hold it firmly in place, so that the board does not move from its position, and check it every day; and whenever it loosens, reset it, and put the board back into its equal position if it has shifted out of place, and lay the patient on their side; and the shoulder is healed in about 20 days or 25, And when these numbers are completed, if it loosens, be sure, for it is not bone that shifts easily."
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	"And if a piece of the bone has come loose, and not reset, so put on top, and the bone, and do as we said in the treatment of the dislocation of the shoulder to calm down an abscess."
de la brisure dou pis	Of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this does not happen often; but it breaks often at the end. And when it is broken in the middle and falls backward, the patient feels great pain, and without support, and always, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the joints in the broken bone, and smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the sick person lies down on his back, and you place a cushion between his shoulders, then press his shoulders together, and join the ribs of the two hands, and carefully make it equal in all ways as much as possible so that the shape of the bone is like this; then wrap it in a cloth, and stick it on the broken bone with plaster, or something light, and wrap it up tightly, and tie it firmly every hour, and if it relaxes, you tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened because corrosion or itching comes to the surface, or pain or swelling comes, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and treat it in a manner appropriate to the cure; then wrap the plaster on again, and tie it tightly until it is well.
de la brisure des costes	For the break of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	That the breaker of ribs comes only in large ones after the back, and to the head inside, and does not bend too much for those that are shiny; and the sound is good in the inquiry to the two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And if he restores it so that you make the break even, just as it should be. And then put the plaster on, and tie it with a strap, if you need to do this.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of ribs is declining inside, then the patient feels great pain and aching, as if crying, for the bone is touching the membrane; and he gets dizzy and nauseous, a great deal of blood comes out, and it is a sign of grave illness, and the old ones have put up a great effort.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who serve say that he should administer meat that swells the belly, to push the break toward the outside.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except when the abscesses are hot, unless they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let the skin be well-cured.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we should put vacuums on the spot, to suck out the excess, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, doubt arises that the vacuum might attract the excesses to the spot due to weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that we should cover the spot with another dry and oiled cloth, and place something between the sides to even out the moisture, then it is cured with the cure for plagues, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that protrudes from the flesh, then doubt is in the patient; so it is necessary to split at the top of the rib that is broken, and to put there an instrument for holding the medicine; and then the bone must be split, and pulled lightly, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat with poultices until he is well. And if the abscesses come out, so put them on cloth drenched in oil, and put them in place; and cure while the place where it is necessary for an absces to come, and be gentle on the rib where it must be, until he is well.
de la brisure dou col	of the break at the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when the bones of the neck break, and there is no pain; and also to the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when it is so that there is no pain in either one, and you know if he will be well or not, if you feel his hands soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick them with an needle, if he does not feel it. Know that it is deadly in many dispositions, and that if they are moved and felt, the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient is cured, if cure is put on him.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you can see whether it is healthy or not, if the muscles are soft, and the accident that is in the hands, and on the back, windiness and digestion without will; and when it is revived on its belly, if digestion without will. And when it is revived on its back and it stiffens, it cannot. Know that it is deadly: so I would not work in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, he is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward him if there is an abscess, put oil or mutton fat on the spine, so that it is calmed down; then put on a compress of confortant and drying, and tie it with a ligature, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels the pain, until he is healthy.
