Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are dislocated, cover it with the cure; and break the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, and treat it with ointment of char in the meantime until it is healthy; and if the head of the shoulder is dislocated, it is called the "head of the collarbone", you hold it with your left hand, and put the plaster and plate on it, if you need to do so; then secure it, and if there are any bones that have come out, set them back in place, and cure the wound until it is healthy.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	There was a possibility that the bone of the thigh might be fractured, and if so, that it would only be a small break at the top; let it grow long, and decline to the left side, and there is great pain for the patient in that place, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the setting-right [restoration] is that you extend your hand towards it as long as you are above the break; and know what is the break and its shape; and if the break is at the top, then make it equal in length to that which is in a natural state.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then bring the patient to her stomach, so that the setting-right of that break may be made for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, place it on the plaster, then place a stake of wood or timber upon it, and hold the break so that it does not move; and set the joints on both sides, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes, do not scratch it, as long as the abscess is calm, and put that which we have said before; and then return to the treatment, and hold it so that there is no bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joints are what connects the neck to the top of the shoulder blade, and when it's broken, there are two ways to fix it: either with a wooden dowel or with a metal plate. With the former, you take a piece of wood that is wider than the joint but not so wide as to interfere with movement; then,
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And take two joints of wood that are long and strong, and tie them together at the top, and cut the patient on one side; then lay him down on his back with his arms by his sides, so that he does not move; and have a wooden dowel ready, and then place it under his shoulder blade with a weight on top of it; then take the broken joint and make it even with his hand, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that if you can wake the patient up, you hold his hand on his neck; then order two ministers: one to hold what is on the break even with his hand, and the other to hold down all the joints, and spread them out to their own parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction is too difficult, then stretch one joint out even with the break, and another on top of it, and spread them both out to their own parts; And if the break is near the top of the shoulder blade, then it is necessary to place a wooden dowel gently under the socket, and another one towards the neck, evenly with the break; then make the break even, as it should be, and hold it, unless an abscess appears.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the abscesses come, do not extract them until .vij. days have passed, and put on a bandage of salt and rose oil, as long as the abscesses are calm; then extract them, and the way to extract them is that you put the plaster on the split, then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the lou [elbow]; and wrap him up, and extract it by the joint, and by his arm, so that his arm is in its place of stars, if nothing harms it or if his bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, then use stars, and put on the split a wider and stronger star than the others, and have between each star 1 2 inches of space, and let each star be so large that it passes the split 1 3 times on either side; then extract on the stars, thus as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the plaster on the split, more strongly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the setting of the stars and the extraction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the member broken, and you doubt the abscess hot, leave it tied for seven days, as we have said; then observe each 1 2 days whether the swelling comes or not to the place, or if the redness does not appear at the member because it is too tight. If it does, put plaster on it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if such an accident does not occur, do not remove the shoulder unless it has been three or more days, and let the patient sleep on his back with his hands on his stomach; and place the aid between the toes of the foot, evenly, and watch every hour of the day or night to make sure that the figure of the broken limb does not move or become softer; if so, treat it by the virtue of medicine, and give him meat as we have said before, in such a way that the meat is at the first level; and when he begins to improve, let it be thick. It is customary that the aid and leg should be removed after ten months; then you must remove it and administer bath and medicines for the application of oil. And if the rigor is ugly and blocked, do not remove it until one or two months have passed.
de la brisure du bras	Of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one being small, and that one is attached to the wrist; and the other is large, and that one is attached at the shoulder. Perhaps one or both of these bones may break, either by itself alone, or together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fire is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the great one is broken, it is bad healing, and more painful than when it is broken all together. If it is only the small fire that is broken, then what is right to do is to extend it lightly, and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the great fire that needs to be stretched more; and extend it on .i. cussin, and darken the pouchet of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the others, and let the patient cross themselves over him in the middle, and .i. cussin in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers by their arms to the part where their hand is, or a .i. ligature, and other ministers on top of them. And then make the pouchet even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, then place each one in its place, and if any of them do not want to hold on to the three, and you cannot reset it in its place, then put it on top of the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break, I have spoken about it to the singular chapter; so take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the treatment there are abscesses, then use a poultice made of oil rosin and white wax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and place it gently above the abscess until the swelling has subsided. And then remove the rosin, and put the plaster of the powder from the mill with much egg, and put the bandages on, and let the break be a little wider than the others; and know that there should be vj. bandages or more in various places: whether the break is in one bone, or in two; and stretch it more above the break than anywhere else, and always less as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread that is stretched from linen be neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And treat the limb and the ligature after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. And if some bad accident comes to the member, as itch that comes to the member, then it is necessary that you soak the member with hot water until the itching has subsided; and let the member rest without being too tight. And then start again with the stretching, and if the ligature is soft and the bone has moved, and similar things, then adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the stretching should not come to the member, because it is too tight, then make it soft a little way, and leave it thus for some days, until the stretching comes, and then stretch it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then he will not be able until .xx. days; or if they do not heal, then he will hold his hands to his neck, and make his neck even, and guard against movement and turning over, and sleep on his back; and know that this bruiser is healed in .xxx. days or in .xxxv. days, and perhaps in .xx. days according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and on our two hands there are few fractures, and come only that many times.

Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks on one of the two legs, so that it is even, so that you tie it up, as is right; and tie it with the plant, and if you see that there is a small right string to raise the break, so that it does not move; and if it breaks on the other leg, so that it is even, and tie it up with the healthy leg that comes after; or tie them all together, holding back, so that they do not hurt each other, or put a string on it, as I have said; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the aposteme, and help those who come to mind, as I said.

And if the fracture is near the root of the groin, then so is one of the links on his side, and the others beside the fracture; and if it is near the knee, then so are the links on either side of the knee, and the extension downward; then put the mirror to the bone equally with both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster on, and tie it up, so that the chas do not come.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a chausie, then let it be calm and return to your work and your cure; the work is done in some way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture i . e. a bandage of tough twine in ii or iii joints, and wait for the excess fluid, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the birth, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, releasing the knee joint, and bring the head with the thread above; then turn on the leg and bandage, then put on the fracture braces, and put a brace on the bone of the leg; then use the stretch between the leg and the thigh of drapeels so that it is equal to the compression, then begin to bind form ii or iii twists on the fracture; and when you go up more on the fracture, and less the compression; then tie the 2 braces that are above, then return to the release at the head of the thread, until you come off from the foot; and let it be so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, and if he comes no fever or swelling or any other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it lets go and turns this way or that, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that hold, if it is possible to do so, yes; and if it is not possible, if it is necessary to split the place and draw out firmly; and cure it as we have said, until he is well.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never does the thigh break in this way when we put braces on it, as in the aid and at the arm; however, in the restoration in this way done does not alarm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the cure is completed within a day, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the neck down
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Saiches that in the neck area there is sometimes a fracture, but it often heals many times. And if it breaks, let it be only a crack or a hole, and not a wound, for this feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the restoration be such that what is broken at both ends is made equal, as much as it can be; then put the plaster on, and put a round stake, if you need one, and hold it in place as it should be, and follow all the dispositions we have said for other breaks, such as an aposteme, and others that seem necessary; and let each accident have what is needed to be healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Saiches that in the leg there are .ij. bones, of which one is called by right "mustelz" and the others are called "foscile"; and all other breaks are similar to those of the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done as with that of the arm equally, and the workings are all alike.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones break together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone breaks, then it turns forwards.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, so that one feels great pain and sees it well; then return to dislocation. Then prepare an extension, and make it even, and tie the stars evenly; but, nevertheless, it is fitting that the fracture should be ugly, and it has more pieces, so that the extension should be smaller and lighter; and make it even according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, so take 30 pieces of rope that color the leg on one side and another, and let them be long from the ankle up to the dislocation; then wrap them in 31 bands above and below, and bind it firmly in the middle, and at this binding cannot move the leg to the right or left, and so is good; and no one administer 30 bands of rope, and if it is rope, and put on the leg to prevent movement, and properly do this in the fracture or there is a sore; and stir each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or another accident; if heal as long as he is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but the bone of the foot comes in several fractures and in two places, and it happens only that it is broken in more than one way.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it should happen that the bones of your foot are broken and you see these bones overtopping one another, then put this patient down upon the earth as if he would walk, and now place your foot upon his own, where the bones are raised up again, then press them together as much as they will go back into their places; then place the plaster and fill it in, and put a small table of 10.5 inches square at the bottom of your foot, then fasten it to the front of the foot, then you have wrapped your drapes and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, then lift up the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two are broken, then reset them, as we have said for the hands; then put a small piece of wood between the two according to their length, and make it one size larger, then put the little table on the foot as I said, and strain it forward; and if there are more than three or four pieces broken, then each one should have a piece of wood according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen drape, and the table should be straining behind the foot; and let it hang down from the top of the table so that it covers the foot well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things that I said for breaking things; and attend to each injury as it occurs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	from breaking of the bone with a knuckle
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is broken in the nature of a woman, if she is sat up enlarged, then she is tilted to the part of the back, and held behind; then fill the bail with cotton, and put there as much as 40 pounds; then turn the woman over, and tap the back little by little, and then drop the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the pound; and when she goes to piss, if she holds the cotton, and when she has pissed, let her put it back again, and so do 15 days or more: then will be restored the break, and if she is dead, take a bladder of lamb, and tie a chain to the crotch, and pour all the bladder into the nature; then blow in the chain shaping, until the bladder is gone inside: the nature will then return the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the knuckle bone of the man or woman is broken, if it is restored as we have said in the bone of the thigh; and these breakages are not hidden from him who puts his study and use thereon, and listens to my book. For the break, therefore, signifies many things in the right way of restoration: hear it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the hymen, when it is broken, take an oiled goose and pour the oil onto the hymen; then wrap drapes around, and leave them 2-3 days or more, and it will be healed in hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	from rupture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For those who have a fracture with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, let it be healed now, so that the healing that we have described serves as a witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, unless there is another injury, then begin to restore the fracture in this same hour, or that very day, for the bones of the hip and shoulder or similar do not heal quickly.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the bones begin to heal, do not continue the restoration work until the next day, provided that the bones are calm and there is no pain; for you would bring about a bad accident if you worked on them for three or four days.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if his nose is broken, it appears on both sides of the bridge; so that you should put it gently with your hands to extend it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not align your hands so that they are equal in length, take this instrument made of iron, which has 2.5 inches or 3 inches of length, and its thickness is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this it is necessary that he immerse himself in mirrhe that he takes 3 or 4 drops, according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member at your touch, and be sharp before, and thick in the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", because the head of the shoulder that is dislocated must be placed on the top of the bone; and tap once, until he recovers, and make them equal one to another. And if the fracture is slight, and the instrument cannot take the bone well, you must cut the top of the bone until the instrument can take it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, with an appropriate instrument, or chisel or saw, in your power; then cut this one that remains in the bone of roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is set back in place, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. If it is in its natural position, then soak it. I.e., wrap it in black wine-styptic cloth, and make sure it is clean; and do not put any tar or other oil on it where there is oil, so that it does not cause pus and corruption to come forth; then administer balsam when you have set the bone back in place, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not tightened with the break; and many times this has been done to the sick, both those who are dead or corroded; and the ligatures are softer and more gentle than others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that an accident has not come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, then it does not suit you to put on esteles; but wrap them up hard, in place of esteles, with tough wraps, and tie them. And when you see after 1 day or 2 days a bow come to the wound, if you take off what you have put on it all wet, and apply healing ointments, as healing tetrafarcion and others.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the limb 2 times a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and whole.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs are arranged in such a way that the bow moves down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if someone runs and cannot fix it but comes together again like this, knowing that there are small pieces of bone, you should put a wound on it, and remove all these painful pieces.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula appears at the place or any other corruption, you should treat it according to what he said in his chapter above. And when the bone is broken and opens on the limb, as the bone of the hip or shoulder, and similar bones of large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times death comes from it, but let it rot; perhaps after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	And the bruses that come out of the ground:
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come back again to the health of the broken, most especially when it is near the joint, and it is a foul sight to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps cannot make its natural movements.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that we come back to the health of the broken, most especially when it is near the joint, and it is a foul sight to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps cannot make its natural movements.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and remains after weak and thin members for some causes: because one is too tied up, and was not tied up so as it should be; or because there are too many joints, and cannot come to the member's aid; or because of many injuries; or because of too great movements, not in its time; or because he has little blood in his body, so weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the torso soft, as many times as the sun rises in him; and he bathes it, and gives it pleasure and joy; then put wax on the member, so that the wax attracts his great swelling, and he rinses it often with warm water, until the swelling corre to the member; and return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the tortured member after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the bone is broken, and the form of the member is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural work: do not believe the foolish who say that one should break the member all over again, and many fools have done this in our land; and such works are blamed, and great harm and even death may result; however, if the nodules and tortures are fresh, it is good to bathe them with hot water, or with soft herbs boiled, such as lamb's ذيل، and melilot، and similar things; and make an ointment. i.e., a mixture of melilot with lard or oil of sesame, and put the ointment on; or take fat figs, and crush them with hay from colon, and other medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And there is no need to break the bone again to rub it continually and for a long time with moist hands. And move the member every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the stiffness is strong and hardened, just as with a stone, it must be cut with a sharp knife lightly; and put on a leech and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to someone, if it is now brought back into place, then let it not be pulled again.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	Car s'on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c'on le déplace à l'oure qu'il est enflé: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, and the swelling increases, and by chance it is put back in place at its original location; for this does not come well, that one moves it before it has decreased: many times it brings spam and other pains; however, when this happens, take care of the patient, then let him rest, until the abscess has calmed down; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then move it lightly, and cure each member as the wound heals.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the remedies for dislocations of the shoulder blade until it is completely healed.
des mandibules	The jaw.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole. de la forcelle	of the fork

Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the shoulder is mute in three parts; that which is mute at the rear is called "gilbosite".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If his hunchback came from childhood then he can be cured; if not, there is no cure or recovery for him at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those that come from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of treatment with great words, which do not give any great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have simplified it according to my intention, and I have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the hunchback that comes before the pitch, there is no remedy or health;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and this is the first sentence I will translate for you:
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and so that the patient is extended on his back in an even position and has not had any strain placed on him, so that he does not bleed;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then put 1. tinder to the head on the ground formed, and 1. other at the feet, and tie a knot over the patient's eyes, and 1. other at the ankles, and at the knees, and at the hips;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and the two ministers know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the 2. tinders;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and are well closed, the twig as we have said, and the mirror sets its palms on the spine forming, until he revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if she does not recover with this cure, then take a table of  .iij. arms long, and shove it against the wall, and let the patient lie on his side, and dip the head of the table against the wall, then put the middle of the table on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and let the mirror put its palms on the other head of the table, and press well, until he revives to his place; and if you see this, do it at the turner that turns in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you put .iij. torches at the head of the sick person with an arm long, and between each torch, one above and one below, a palm's space apart;
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and place in each log .i. pierce, or the pole runs, and let the logs firmly be in the ground so that they do not move, and between each two logs let there be one log turning, so that the bond turns, and let there be in each of two turning logs .i. turning pole of a palm long, to turn the pole.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the bond that is between the logs to the pole at the top, and the other bond towards the poles at the other end, and each of the servants turns its bond to all the log, and the master places the stake evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put on desiccant with much ash, and then the stakes, and then the stake of a tablet of a palm long, that by purifying the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then tie a bond of a log, as we have said, and use subtle emollient to him until he is healthy;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if anything comes to an end in the health of it, if necessary administer softening and soothing medicines, with the stake that we have said above; and never administer a piece of lead.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and never comes the appearance behind the spine of the back, and think that it is dislocations; and this bone which opens, so that one should not have presumption: by chance would come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	that the hip and shoulder joints only come with dislocations, not as in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to three.iiij. parties: inside and outside, and before and behind, and more inside, and less before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocations inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is further away, and opens more the sick foot than the healthy one, and cannot bend the sick knee on fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and is the limb which is swollen with feverish heat from an abscess, for the head of the hip comes to lie there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that person who is going to die, if this accident is opposite to those above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that person who is going to die, if this accident is opposite to those above. However, if his leg is well according to the accomplishment; nevertheless, it does not double the knee due to pain, and if he is made to walk, he cannot do so before, and reten
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that person who is going to die, if this accident is opposite to those above. However, if his leg is well according to the accomplishment; nevertheless, it does not double the knee due to pain, and if he is made to walk, he cannot do so before, and reten
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If the dislocation is old and delays according to its habit, there is no cure for it; and it is only right that he should have been presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that which the dislocation is new, and it is of the four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to restore the joint, and turn it inside and out, and move it to the right and to the left; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not come back in this way, you must have very strong help, and firmly support the leg with two hands, or a ligature tied on the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and others extend their hand above him in such a way that they press their hands together, then tie a ligature around his thigh; and others hold the hair of the ligature;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend up and down all at once, as long as the sick person is raised from the ground once, and remain so.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to three resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, then you should put the patient on his back. When the dislocations are in the paregorico position, if it is convenient that you put the sick person on his side, then set the ligature on the root of the hip, and the line that is removed from the angle, then extend the ligature upwards towards the angle, and upwards towards the forceps;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then pull the arms of the sick person, and embrace the large line of the hip, and extend it to the side: so he will return to his position now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot fasten it in this way that we have said, then you must tie the .ij. feet of the patient together with a strong thread under the .ij. heels, and under the .ij. knees, so that the sick leg is longer than the other by .ij. two;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then hang him by the neck of a post, and be above ground 2 arms long; then order 1 minister to embrace the hip of the patient, and let others hang down with the patient, who embrace his hips firmly, because the joints will come back into place quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is far away, if the patient lies down as we have said in the case of gilo-boseity, and draws 1 thread properly on the sick leg, and also on the foot;
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put 2 torches, 1 at the head and 1 at the feet, then put 1 torch between the hips of the patient so that it goes in his middle;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and put on him a wet cloth from behind, that he may not hurt the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and let the doctor set the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that is good. If not, put him on a .ie. table and press him as we said in the gibosity, and lay the patient on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, extend the injured leg outward, and according to what I have said; and let the doctor put his hand on it from behind, then press with the other hand, and raise it towards the hip.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And when the dislocation is on one side, so it is not possible to extend the injured leg outward, nor to raise it towards the hip; then it is necessary that he should lie on his back with both legs outstretched, as we have said in the sleep on the two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and is placed on its face, and the limb extends as we have said above, and must be firmly pressed against the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and will be in place when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; then take the poultice, and put on the plaster, and extract an arrow, so that the shin does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and rests for three days or four, then unbinds it, and puts on the plaster; and if you see that they are even, as before, and leaves it in place. three days; then unbinds it, and lets him bark loudly, until the limbs are comfortable again.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the kneecap
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The genoux is dislocated according to three ways: namely, inward, outward, and rearward; do not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he does not bend it at the knee, that he is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the treatment for all of this is that you make the patient sit upright, and if he can extend his leg, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your legs;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee with your hands, and pull it between your two, then bend the .iij. knees together like a knee; and other ministers extend his foot, until the genoux returns to its place, and the signs are that he has moved his leg at the knee lightly;
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and place the plaster on top of it, and make the leg rest in the lap, and bind it together tightly .iii or .iv days, then remove it; and do not work the patient to walk, as long as the limbs are not comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not in place, then give a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	from the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never fully dislocated or realigned, and they go in and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and test before the part where it has come out.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The following text is the translation of the provided Old French text:
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it has come out completely, so that you make the patient lie down flat on his back, and tie him up by the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	And then try the foot with your right hand, and then with your left hand, and then again with your right hand, and then stretch it out, and blow on the foot well;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this .ij. times, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, then begin again with the work, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	if it cannot return in this way, then have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place 1 pass firmly into the ground between his buttocks, and tie a cloth around it, so that he does not injure the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then put the minister's hand on his buttocks, and another minister extends the foot to his hands or to .i. a cord, so that he lays it on the top of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each minister equally, and place the cloth tight between the patient's buttocks to hold the patient in place while you are working;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then make the patient's dislocated arm equal with his hands, and other ministers will dye the healthy leg with tar, and the dislocation will return completely.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is ready, if you apply the plaster and wrap it up tightly, and form the bandage well, and fasten the foot to the leg, and guard against the tendons behind the ankle being too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	then let it rest for .ij. or .iij., and if the bandage is loose, then untie it after three or four days, and do not send the patient away before .iiij. days have passed;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before that term is up, it is not yet certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form quickly, then it is necessary that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy again.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if it is gently extended without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in the lower back or foot, then it is necessary that you make the patient sit down on a bed or table all straight, and place your foot on what opens up these joints, and then press with your foot in this form, until he returns;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when it is even, and there is nothing open, then put the foot on a table of .ij. shoulders, then extract it shaped, and leave it .iiij. days, then unpick it; and let it rest as long as it is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When the wound comes with the dislocation, and it is reset, many times the patient has died:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, you have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and slow to anger, do not be arrogant:
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning of things soothing ointment, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope for health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, so I put back the member in place, that way the soothing ointment will come;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the member is in place, so administer soothing ointment, and cure the wound, as appropriate, with dry compresses;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a dislocation with a fracture, and small bones are broken, if the bones, do as we have said in simple illnesses;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	and keep yourself from entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cost you dear according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming yourself and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Here is the translation:
